The author of this book said: When I completed for you, my son, this book, which is the theoretical part of medicine in its entirety, and reached the limit in its clarity and explanation, I decided to complete it for you with this treatise, which is the practical part, because practical work and its practitioners are completely nonexistent in our country and in our time, so that its knowledge almost disappeared and its impact vanished.
Only minor traces of it remained in the books of the predecessors, which have been distorted by hands and affected by errors and confusion, so that its meanings became obscure and its benefit distant, so I decided to revive it and compose this treatise in the way of explanation, clarification, and brevity, and to provide images of cautery irons and other surgical instruments, as this is an addition to the explanation and among the most important things needed.
The reason why there is no skilled practitioner in our time is that the study of medicine is long, and its student should be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy described by Galen, until he understands the benefits of the organs, their structures, temperaments, connections, separations, knowledge of the bones, nerves, and muscles, their number and exits, and the pulsating and static veins, and the locations of their exits.
Therefore, Hippocrates said that doctors are many in name but few in practice, especially in surgery.
We have mentioned some of this in the introduction of this book, because whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned of anatomy will inevitably fall into an error that kills people with it, as I have seen many of those who imagined themselves knowledgeable in this science and claimed it without knowledge or skill.
This is because I saw an ignorant doctor who incised a scrofulous swelling in a woman's neck, so he pierced some of the arteries of the neck, and the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead between his hands.
And I saw another doctor who proceeded to extract a stone from a man who had been stabbed in the bladder, and the stone was large, so he rushed and extracted it with a piece of the bladder, so the man died after about three days.
I was called to extract it, and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient what I estimated about it.
And I saw another doctor who was earning a living with some of the leaders of our country through medicine, and a black boy who had a fracture in his leg near the heel with a wound happened to be with him, so the doctor hastened in his ignorance and tightly bandaged the fracture over the wound with pads and splints, and he did not leave any breathing space for the wound, then he left him to his desires, then he left him for days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage until his leg and foot swelled and he was near death, so I was called to him, and I quickly loosened the bandage, so he felt relief and recovered from his pains, except that the infection had already taken hold in the limb, and I could not stop it, so the infection continued to spread in the limb until he died.
And I saw another doctor who cauterized a cancerous tumor, so it ulcerated after days until his affliction worsened, and this is because if cancer is purely of melancholic humor, then it should not be exposed to iron at all, unless it is in a limb that can be completely amputated.
Therefore, my son, you should know that surgery is divided into two parts: a safe procedure and a procedure that is harmful in most cases. I have warned in every place that comes from this book about the procedure that has risks and dangers, so you should beware of it and reject it so that the ignorant does not find a way to speak and criticize. Take for yourselves firmness and precaution, and for your patients, gentleness and certainty, and use the best way that leads to safety and a good outcome, and avoid dangerous diseases that are difficult to diagnose, and purify yourselves from what you fear will bring you suspicion in your religion and your world, for it is more lasting for your prestige and higher in this world and the hereafter for your status.
Galen said in some of his advice: Do not treat a bad disease, so you are called bad doctors.
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter is about cauterization with fire and cauterization with strong medicine, organized and arranged from head to toe, with images of instruments, cautery irons, and everything needed for surgery.
The second chapter is about incision, lancing, bloodletting, cupping, surgeries, removing arrows, and so on, all organized and arranged with images of instruments.
The third chapter is about bone setting, dislocations, treatment of tendons, and so on, organized and arranged from head to toe with images of instruments.
The first chapter on cauterization.
And before we mention the procedure with it, it is necessary that we mention the nature of its benefits and harms, and in what temperament it is used.
So I say that the discussion about the nature of the benefit and harm of cautery is a long discussion, a precise science, and a hidden secret, and a group of sages have spoken about it and differed about it.
And I have summarized from their words the little, for fear of prolixity.
So I say that cautery is generally useful for every bad temperament that is with matter and without matter, except for two temperaments, which are the hot temperament without matter and the dry temperament without matter.
As for the dry temperament with matter, they have differed about it, so some of them said that cautery is beneficial in it, and others said the opposite of that, that cautery is not suitable for a disease that is from heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat and dryness, and it is impossible to be cured from a hot dry disease with a hot dry remedy.
And the one who says the opposite of that said that cautery with fire may benefit from a hot dry disease that occurs in people's bodies, because when you add the human body and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I say according to his saying because experience has revealed that to me many times, except that it is not appropriate for anyone to imagine about that matter except one who has practiced and trained in the field of cautery with extensive training and has observed the difference in people's temperaments and the state of diseases in themselves, their causes, their symptoms, and their duration.
And as for the other temperaments, there is no fear for you from them, especially the cold, moist diseases, for all the physicians have agreed on them and have not differed about the benefit of cautery in them.
And know, my sons, that among the secrets of treatment is cautery with fire, and its superiority over cautery with burning medicine, because fire is a simple substance whose action does not exceed the organ that is cauterized, and it does not harm another organ connected to it except with slight harm.
And cautery with burning medicine, its action may extend to what is beyond the organs, and perhaps it causes in the organ a disease whose treatment is difficult, and perhaps it kills.
And fire, due to its nobility and the generosity of its substance, does not do that unless it is excessive.
And that has become clear to us through experience, due to the length of service and care for the craft and observing the realities of the matter, and for this reason I have dispensed with lengthy speech.
And were it not that it is not appropriate for this book of mine, I would have presented to you regarding fire a mysterious secret and the nature of its action in bodies and its expulsion of diseases, with philosophical, demonstrative words that are too subtle for your understanding.
And know, my sons, that they have differed about the time in which cautery is suitable, and they have considered the best time to be the time of spring.
And I say that cautery may be suitable in every time, because the harm that occurs from the time is absorbed in the benefit that is brought about by cautery, especially if the cautery is for necessary, strong, urgent pains that do not tolerate delay, because it is feared that they will be followed by a calamity that is greater than the slight harm that comes from the time.
And do not let it occur to your minds, my sons, what the common people and ignorant physicians imagine, that the cautery that cures from a certain disease will never return, and you consider it blameworthy.
And the matter is not as you thought, because cautery is just like the medicine that alters the temperament and dries the moistures that are the cause of the occurrence of pains, except that cautery is superior to medicine in the speed of its success, the strength of its action, and the intensity of its power.
And it is possible that the disease will return at some point in time, depending on the temperament of the patient, the establishment of his disease, its strength, and what is prepared in his body from the accumulation of superfluities in it, and his neglect of himself in acquiring them from foods and such causes.
However, unless the disease in which cautery is used is a mild disease and in an organ with few superfluities and moistures, such as cauterizing the tooth for pain and the like, it is possible that the pain will not return in it, and that is in the minority of cases.
And as for the saying of the common people also that cautery is the last of medicine, it is a correct saying, not in what they mean, because they believe that no treatment is beneficial with medicine or otherwise after cautery occurs, and the matter is contrary to that, but rather the meaning that cautery is the last of medicine is that when we use various types of treatment for a disease and those medicines do not work, then we use the last thing, cautery, and it works, so from here it happens that cautery is the last of medicine, not in the sense that the common people and many of the ignorant physicians mean.
And the ancients have mentioned that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they only said that because of the moderation of gold and the nobility of its substance, and they said that the place of cautery does not suppurate, and that is not absolute, because I have tried that and found it only does that in some bodies and not others, and cautery with it is better and superior to iron, as they said, except that if you heat the cautery iron in the fire from gold, it will not be clear to you when it heats to the extent that you want, due to the redness of gold, and because coldness quickly affects it, and if you increase the heating on it, it melts in the fire and flows, so the craftsman falls into trouble because of that, so therefore cautery with iron is faster for us and closer to correctness for the procedure, God willing.
And I have arranged this chapter on cautery into sections that I have organized from head to toe, to facilitate for the student what he wants from it, God willing.
The first chapter on cauterizing the head with one cauterization.
This cauterization is beneficial for excess moisture and coldness on the brain, which are the cause of headaches, frequent catarrh from the head towards the eyes and ears, excessive sleep, toothache, throat aches, and in general, for every disease that arises from coldness, such as paralysis, epilepsy, muteness, and similar ailments.
The method of this cauterization is that you first order the patient to vomit using a purgative medicine that cleanses the head for three or four nights, depending on the patient's strength, age, and habit. Then you order him to shave his head with a razor, then sit him cross-legged between your hands, having placed his hands on his chest. Then you place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his eyes. Where your middle finger ends, mark that place with ink. Then heat the olive-shaped cautery, which is like this:
Expose from the bone the size of a toothpick head or the size of a cherry pit, then lift your hand. Otherwise, repeat with the same iron or another one if it has cooled down, until you see the bone as I mentioned to you. Then take some salt, dissolve it in water, soak cotton in it, place it on the spot, and leave it for three days. Then apply cotton soaked in ghee and leave it on until the burn from the fire disappears. Then treat it with the quadruple ointment until he recovers, God willing.
They have said that the longer the wound remains open and suppurates, the better and more beneficial it is.
Some have mentioned that the skin should be cauterized to the bone, and the cautery should be held until some of the thickness of the bone is burned. Then the burned part of the bone is scraped, and then treated.
Others have said that the cauterization should be exaggerated until it has a strong effect on the bone, so that something like a carat or a small disk falls off the bone. They claimed that it vents the vapors of the head from that place, and the wound is left open for a long time, then treated until it heals.
I do not see these two types of cautery at all except in some people, and by way of risk, and leaving it is better in my opinion. And safety, if it exists, is because the head weakens when its natural connection is severed, as we have seen in other organs, especially when the patient's head is naturally weak. The first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it, so work with it, and you will be safe, God willing.
The second chapter on cauterizing the head also.
If a chronic headache occurs and it lasts for the patient, and he has used eardrops, sternutatories, nasal instillations, ointments, and bandages, especially if he has been cauterized with the single cautery that we described, and none of that benefited him, then consider: If the patient's head is naturally strong in constitution, and he is not weak, and he feels intense cold, then cauterize him with another cautery slightly above that one. ثمّ اكوه على كلّ قرن من رأسه كيّة حتّى يذهب ثخن الجلد وينكشف من العظم القدر الذى وصفنا
And I will mention this cautery in its place.
It is appropriate that the cautery iron used to cauterize the horns of the head and its back be gentler than the cautery iron used to cauterize the middle of the head.
The third chapter on cauterizing non-chronic migraine.
If pain occurs in the fissure of the head along with a headache, and the pain extends to the eye, then induce vomiting in the patient with medicines that purify the head, and employ all the other treatments that I mentioned in the classification of diseases. فإن لم ينجع ذلك فالكىّ فيها على وجهين
As for cauterization with a burning medication, it is that you take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. ثمّ شقّ موضع الوجع من الصدغ بمبضع عريض حتّى يصير فيه موضعا تحت الجلد يسع فيه السنّ فيدخل فيه تحت الجلد حتّى يغيب
Then tighten it with a bandage, tightly, and leave it for about fifteen hours. ثمّ حلّه وأخرج الثوم واترك الجرح يومين او ثلثة
Then treat it with the ointment until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, you can do this with some of the burning medications that I provided in the eighteenth article on burning medications.
And as for cauterizing it with iron, it is in this manner: you heat the cautery iron, which is of this form:
And it is called the nail-shaped cautery because its head is like the shape of a nail, with some curvature and a small protrusion in its middle.
Then you place it on the painful area and hold your hand while you rotate the iron little by little.
And the amount you burn of the skin's thickness should be like half of it, and you lift your hand so as not to burn the artery that is underneath, causing bleeding.
Then you soak cotton in salt water and place it on the area and leave it for three days, then you load the cotton with ghee, then you treat it with the ointment until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, cauterize this migraine with the knife-like edge coming from the cautery, and be careful of cutting the artery in this migraine, especially if it's not chronic.
Chapter four on cauterizing chronic migraine.
If you treat migraine with the aforementioned advanced treatment and what we mentioned in the classification of diseases, and the treatment does not work, and you see that the ailment is not resolved by what we mentioned of the first cauterization with medicine or cauterization with fire, then it is necessary to heat the knife-shaped cautery iron until it becomes white after marking the painful area with a line half a finger long or so, and you withdraw your hand at once while pulling it tight until you cut the artery and reach the bone, except that you should be careful of contacting the jaw that moves during chewing, lest you burn the muscle or the nerve that moves it, causing spasm.
Be careful and vigilant about bleeding from the artery that you cut, as there is danger in cutting it, especially for those who are ignorant of what they are doing and have not been trained and experienced, and it is better to leave the procedure.
The management of accidental bleeding from the artery will be mentioned in its place in the book, God willing.
If you find that the ailment is not resolved by this cauterization and you see that the patient's body can tolerate it, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we described, and treat the wound until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, use the cauterization that we mentioned in the chapter on dissecting the artery with the two-bladed cautery iron, for it is a better and more effective cauterization than this.

If there occurs in the ear pain from cold. وعولج بالمسهلات وسائر العلاج الذى ذكرنا فى التقسيم ولم يذهب الوجع.
Then you apply drops with it, after heating it, around the entire ear as you go around, or around both of them if the pain is in both. وتبعد بالكىّ من أصل الأذن قليلا بعد أن تعلّم الموضع بالمداد
And the cautery should be the size of ten dots in each ear, or about that.
Then you treat the places until they heal, God willing.
Chapter Six on Cauterizing the Jaw Muscle.
The facial paralysis that is treated with cautery is of the type that arises from phlegm, as I mentioned in the classification of diseases.
And avoid cauterizing the type that arises from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this type of facial paralysis with errhines, sternutatories, and gargles, and your treatment does not succeed, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one at the base of the ear, the second a little below his temple, and the third at the joining of the lips.
And make your cauterization on the opposite side of the affected area, because the relaxation occurs on the side that appears healthy.
And the method of cautery is to cauterize with a cautery opposite the upper tip of the ear, a little below the horn of the head, and another on the temple, and its length should be the length of the thumb. تنزل بالكّى يدك حتّى تحرق قدر نصف ثخن الجلد،
And this is the image of the cautery instrument, and it is a type of scalpel-like instrument whose image has been presented, except that it is a little gentler, as you see.
And the knife should have a little extra thickness.
Then treat the area with what was mentioned previously until it heals, God willing.
The seventh chapter on cauterizing chronic stroke.
If the stroke becomes chronic and you have treated it with what we have mentioned, and your treatment has not been successful, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauterizations, one on each side of his head. وكيّة فى وسط الرأس كما ذكرنا
And the description of the cauteries is as previously mentioned.
And he may also be cauterized at the pit of the stomach, which would be more effective.
Then treat with what has been previously mentioned.
The eighth chapter on cauterizing forgetfulness that is caused by phlegm.
The patient should first be given to drink from the major electuaries and brain-purifying pills.
Then his entire head should be shaved. وتحمل على مؤخّره ضماد الخردل المكتوب فى مقالة الاضمدة
Apply it several times, for it is a kind of cautery. وافعل ذلك على الرتبة بعينها التى ذكرتها هنالك
If he is cured by that, then fine, otherwise cauterize him with three cauterizations on the back of his head, aligned from the top of the head to the bottom of the neck. واجعل بين كلّ كيّة وكيّة غلظ اصبع
Then treat the cautery with what was mentioned previously.
If you want to increase it, and the patient can tolerate it, cauterize the middle cauterization. فإن اردت الزيادة فاكوه على القرنين
Then treat him until he recovers.

Chapter nine on cauterizing paralysis and the relaxation of the entire body.
It is necessary to proceed in purifying the head with the irriagations and what we have mentioned.

The tenth chapter on cauterizing epilepsy.
Only cauterize the epileptic whose epilepsy is caused by phlegm.
It is necessary to first purify his brain with major purges and with all the treatments that we mentioned in the section if the patient is an adult and can tolerate taking medications.
But if he is a child who cannot tolerate the medications, then he should use gargles and masticatories that purify the brain for many days before that, along with improving his nutrition, then shave his head, then cauterize him with a single cauterization in the middle of the head as described previously, and another cauterization on his posterior, and a cauterization on each side of his head.
If the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize him with the cauterizations that were mentioned for the one with paralysis and body relaxation on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
And the cautery iron should be olive-shaped according to the description that was presented earlier.

Chapter eleven on cauterizing melancholia
If the cause of melancholia is corrupt humors and thick phlegm, cauterize him with the cauterizations that we mentioned for the stroke patient.
And if the cause of melancholia is an excess inclining towards black bile, and the patient's body is moist, give him to drink what purifies his brain as mentioned previously in the classification. ثمّ احلق رأس العليل
Then make a well-sealed ring-like cake of linen. ثمّ أنزلها فى وسط رأسه والعليل قاعد متربّعا يمسك من كلّ جهة
Then take one pound of old sheep fat. ثمّ سخّنه على النار سخونة معتدلة قدر ما يحتمل الاصبع اذا أدخل فيه
Do this to the patient once every week, along with all his other good management, until he recovers, God willing.
And if you wish, cauterize him with many small, dotted cauterizations, without holding your hand on the cautery iron, but rather with a quick touch.
For this type of cauterization moistens the brain moderately.
Then apply cotton soaked in the fat or in chicken fat.
The twelfth chapter on cauterizing the water descending into the eye.
If the beginning of the descending water in the eye is clear to you by the signs that were mentioned in the classification, then hasten to give the sick person what purifies his head, and protect him from all moistures, and make him sweat in the bath on an empty stomach for days.
Then order him to shave his head and cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head. ثمّ اكوه كيّتين على الصدغين إن كان ابتداء نزول الماء فى العينين جميعا او من الجانب الواحد إن كان فى العين الواحدة.
Then cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin, and let the cauteries be long across the width of the temples, and beware of bleeding, so if you see any of it, stop it immediately with any treatment you can, and we will come to the wisdom in stripping the arteries and cutting them and guarding against bleeding.
And he may be cauterized on the nape of the neck under the two bones with two deep cauteries.

Chapter fifteen on cauterizing the relaxation of the eyelid.
If the eyelid becomes flaccid due to illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid once with this crescent-shaped cautery iron.
And if you wish, cauterize him slightly above the eyebrows, two cauterizations on each side, and keep away from the temples. ويكون طول كلّ كيّة على طول الحاجب
And do not overdo your hand with the cautery, but only to the extent that a third of the skin is burned.
And the shape of the cautery iron should be according to this description.
Chapter sixteen on cauterizing the eyelid if its lashes turn inwards and prick the eye.
So cauterization in it is of two types: either cauterization by fire or cauterization by a burning medication.
As for cauterizing it with fire, you order the patient, before that, to leave his eyelashes, if he is among those who pluck them, until they grow long and even. فإن نخسته عند نباتها فتشدّ عينيه بعصابة لئلّا تتحرّك حتّى تنبت
When they have grown and are even, place the patient's head in your lap. ثمّ تعلّم على جفن العين بالمداد علامة على شكل ورقة آس
Then you place under the eyelid cotton soaked in egg white or in psyllium seed mucilage.
Then you heat a cautery iron, this is its image:
Then cauterize on the shape that you marked, little by little, in many times until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is completely burned, especially its surface.
And the sign of the correctness of your work is that you see the eyelid has curled up and the hair has risen from the flesh of the eye, so lift your hand then and leave it for three days.
Then apply cotton with ghee on it until the eschar falls off, then treat it with the ointment until it heals, God willing.
If any of the hair returns after a while and the eyelid relaxes, repeat the cauterization on that place as you did first.
If the hair is on the lower eyelid, cauterize it until it returns to its natural position and the hair does not prick the eye.
As for cauterization with the burning medication, it is that you order the patient to leave the eyelashes until they grow long and even, then you make from paper the shape of a myrtle leaf, then take from the usual soap and from the quicklime, not slaked, of each one the weight of a dirham or so, and you grind them both well, and you do that quickly lest it dry, then you spread it on the paper that you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf and place it on the eyelid of one or both eyes, and you place under the eye cotton soaked in egg white, and the patient's head in your lap, and you place your index finger over the medication and press it slightly while moving it whenever the patient feels the sting of the medication, because he feels a sting like fire, so as long as he feels the sting, leave the medication and move it with your finger, and when the sting subsides, remove the medication and wash the eye with water and look. If you see the eyelid has risen as it rises when curling with fire or cutting, otherwise, reapply some of the medication on the area where the medication did not affect and did not blacken until you complete your work and the eye curls up, then place cotton with ghee on it until the burning scab falls off, then treat it with the palm ointment or another until it heals.
And it is necessary for you, when working, to be extremely careful that nothing of the medication falls into the eye.
If the eyelid relaxes after days and we fear something from the hair in the eye, reapply the medication on that area of the eyelid that relaxed, specifically as you did first, then treat it until it heals.
And this is a picture of a myrtle leaf:
And know that people's eyes may differ in smallness and largeness. فعلى حسب ذلك فليكن تشميرك
And the correct way is not hidden from one who has practice in this profession.
The seventeenth chapter on cauterizing the fistula that appears in the corner of the eye.
If you treated the fistula with what we mentioned in the classifications of diseases and your treatment was not successful, then it should be cauterized in this manner.
You order the patient to place his head in your lap, and an assistant holds his head between your hands, holding it firmly so that he does not move or shake his head.
Then you place cotton moistened in egg white or in psyllium mucilage on his eyes.
Then you heat the cautery iron, which is of this shape:
It should be hollow, like the quill of an eagle's feather, from the one end which will be cauterized.
And if you wish, it can be perforated at the other end. وإن شئت كانت مصمتة كالمرود
But this hollow one is better for your work, God willing.
Then squeeze the fistula if it is open and remove the pus and dry it. او كان غير مفتوح فتفتحه وتستخرج قيحه
Then apply the cautery, which is very hot. فتمسك بها يدك حتّى تصل الى العظم
And move your hand a little during cauterization from the eye towards the nose, lest your hand err or the patient fidget, and the cautery falls into the eyelid and damages it.
If it reaches the bone with the first cauterization, وإلّا فأعد المكواة مرّة ثانية إن احتجت الى ذلك
And leave it for three days. ثمّ احمل عليه قطنة بالسمن وعالجه بالمرهم المجفّف حتّى يبرأ،
If forty days pass and it does not heal, then apply a strong corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed. واجرده على ما سيأتى ذكره فى بابه إن شاء الله،
And another method of cauterizing the fistula, mentioned by some of the ancients, تعمد الى موضع الناصور تشقّه ثم تضع فى نفس الشقّ قمعا رقيقا هذه صورته:
And it is advisable that you place on the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white or in water.
For the lead cauterizes the fistula's location and heals it wonderfully.
If the fistula is healed by what we have mentioned of cauterization and treatment, then good; otherwise, it is necessary to use perforation of the nose and return the fistula to the nasal passage as will come in its specific place.
Chapter Eighteen on Cauterizing Cleft Lip
Often there occurs a fissure in the lip called the hair. ولا سيّما فى شفاه الصبيان فإنّه كثيرا ما يحدث.
If you treat this fissure with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment does not succeed, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery in this way:
Its depth should be as thin as a knife.
Then you place it hot, quickly, in the same fissure. حتّى يصل الكىّ الى عمق الشقاق
Then you treat it with cerate until it heals, God willing.
Chapter nineteen on cauterizing fistula occurring in the mouth.
If a swelling appears in the gums' origin or in the palate or in the roots of the molars. ثمّ قاح وانفجر وصار من جرى القيح ناصور

Chapter twenty on cauterizing the molars and the relaxed gums.
If the gums are loose due to moisture and the molars are loose, and you have treated them with medicines and they have not been effective, then place the patient's head in your lap.
Then heat the cautery iron, whose image comes after this, after you place the tube on the tooth and insert the hot cautery iron into it quickly and hold your hand for a short time until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth. ثّم ترفع يدك
Then repeat the cautery as many times as you want.
Then the patient fills his mouth with salt water and holds it for an hour and then spits it out.
For the loose tooth will be fixed, and the loose gums will tighten, and the corrupt moisture will dry up.
Chapter twenty-one on cauterizing toothache.
If the toothache is caused by cold or there are worms in it, and treatment with medicines is not effective, then cauterization is done in two ways: either cauterization with ghee or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with ghee is done by taking cow ghee and boiling it in an iron spoon or in a shell, then taking cotton and wrapping it around the tip of a probe, then dipping it in the boiling ghee and placing it quickly on the aching tooth, holding it until it cools, and repeating this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
If you wish, you can dip wool or cotton in cold ghee and place it on the aching tooth and place the heated iron on top of it until the heat reaches the bottom of the tooth.
Cauterization with fire is done by using a copper or iron tube that is somewhat thick so that the heat of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
Then, heat the cauterizing iron, the image of which is shown, and place it on the tooth itself, holding your hand steady until the iron cools. Repeat this several times and the pain will go away, either that same day or the next.
After the cauterization, the patient should fill his mouth with good ghee, hold it for an hour, and then spit it out.
And this is the image of the cauterizing iron:
Cauterize with whichever end you wish and according to what is possible.
And this is a picture of the tube:

Perforated at both ends so that the smoke may come out of the other end during cauterization.

If the tumor is small, make the cautery iron the size of the tumor.
Then leave it for three days and apply cotton dipped in fat on it until what was burned by the fire disappears.
Then treat it with the ointment and wicks until it heals, God willing.
Chapter twenty-three on cauterization for hoarseness of voice and shortness of breath.
If moistures prevail over the trachea, especially if that is with a cold temperament, then the sick person should first vomit using laxative medications.
Then cauterize him with a cautery in the pit of the jugular vein at the base of the larynx in the low place, but be careful not to reach the larynx with the cautery, and do not burn more than half of the skin.
Then cauterize him with another cautery at the joint of the neck at the last vertebra of it, intensely, and the cautery should be nail-shaped according to the description that preceded.
Then treat him with what was mentioned previously until he recovers, God willing.
Chapter twenty-four on cauterizing lung disease and cough.
If the cough and lung disease are due to cold humors, and the patient has neither fever nor phthisis, and the disease is chronic, then cauterize him with two cauterizations above the clavicles in the low, soft, empty places, and another cauterization in the middle of the chest between the breasts, and the cautery iron should be nail-shaped in the form that has been previously described.
And if you wish, let your cauterization be by spotting with the cautery iron that is called "the point," and its form has been previously described in the spotting for earache, and the spots should be from thirty spots to about that number.

And a cautery iron with three prongs may be made in this form, and cauterization is hastened with it because you cauterize three cauterizations with it at once.

Chapter twenty-eight on treating liver swelling with cauterization.
If an abscess appears in the liver and you want to know whether that swelling is in the liver's parenchyma or in its membrane, then if it is in the parenchyma, the patient will feel heaviness and pain without sharpness.
And if it is in the liver's membrane, there will be intense sharpness with the pain. ورأيت أنّه قد أعيا الأطبّاء علاجه فينبغى أن يستلقى العليل على قفاه
And I have seen that its treatment has baffled physicians, so the patient should lie on his back. ثمّ تعلّم على الموضع الوارم بالمداد

Then treat it with the treatment of abscesses until it heals.
And this type of cauterization should not be used except by someone who has long training in the art of medicine and has treated these diseases with experience repeatedly.
Only then should he undertake such a procedure.
And leaving it (untreated) in my opinion is better.
Chapter twenty-nine on cauterizing hemorrhoids.

And it is not appropriate to deepen your hand with the cautery, rather it should be on the surface of the skin, a superficial burning.

And in this recklessness with cautery is a great risk: either the patient dies immediately, or a fistula develops in the area that has no cure.
Chapter Thirty on Cauterizing the Spleen
If you treat a disease of the spleen with the treatment we mentioned in the division and your treatment does not succeed, then cauterizing it has three aspects, all of which are correct, one of which is to cauterize it three or four cauterizations aligned along the length of the spleen, in the form of liver cauterizations, whose form we presented previously, and the space between each cauterization should be the width of a finger or slightly more, and the character of the cautery iron is the same character that we mentioned in the cauterization of the liver, and do not deepen your hand with the cautery, and the image of the sick person is lying on his back.
And the other aspect is in the elbow, and you lift the skin opposite the spleen where the elbow of the sick person ends, the elbow, and you lift the skin opposite the spleen where the left elbow of the sick person ends, and your lifting of the skin should be across the width of the body, so that the cauterizations fall along the length of the body, then you insert the two skewers, very protected, until they penetrate the skin from the other side, then you remove the cautery iron, so the cauterizations are four.
And if you wish to cauterize with the other cautery iron, which has three skewers, then treat the cauterized area after you leave it to drain pus for many days, then it is more effective than all of what preceded from the treatment.
Chapter thirty-one on cauterizing ascites.
Cauterization is only beneficial in particular for ascites due to an obstruction.
If you treat the patient with ascites with the types of treatment that we mentioned in the classification, and your treatment is not effective, then it is appropriate to cauterize him with four cauterizations around the navel, one cauterization on the stomach, another cauterization on the liver, a cauterization on the spleen, and two cauterizations behind his back between the vertebrae, one facing his chest and the other facing his stomach. ويكون قدر عمق الكىّ قريبا من ثخن الجلد،
Then you leave the cauterization open, letting the pus flow for a long time.
And do not neglect treating the patient after the cauterization with what is appropriate to combine for him the two meanings, so that healing will quickly come to him.
And the shape of the cautery iron with which the back is cauterized should be nail-shaped, as its image was presented previously, and the one with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped.

Then treat it with all that we have mentioned.
Chapter thirty-three on cauterizing diarrhea.
If the diarrhea is from cold and humors, so that it weakens the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines, and it has been treated with various treatments, but has not healed, and you see the patient tolerating cautery and having sufficient strength, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, as mentioned previously in cauterizing the stomach with the circular cautery iron, and four gentle cauterizations around the navel with the gentle nail-shaped cautery iron, and a large cautery on the coccyx above the buttocks, or two cauteries.
If you see that the humors are abundant and the patient can tolerate it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the pubis and a cautery on each flank, and perhaps you may add two small cauterizations on the stomach near the large one, for it is a successful treatment whose benefit will not fail, God willing.

Chapter thirty-five on cauterizing warts after cutting them.

Chapter Thirty-Six on Cauterizing the Fistula that Occurs in the Anus and its Surroundings
If the patient does not respond to the incision and the procedure that we described in its place and is afraid of it, then perhaps he will recover with cauterization.
So if a fistula occurs in someone and becomes chronic, pus and corrupted fluids flow from it, then the first thing you should do is measure it with a thin probe. ثمّ اعرف قدر غوره بالمسبار
Then heat the cauterizing iron that resembles the probe. ثم أدخلها حامية فى نفس الناصور على استقامة غور الناصور والقدر الذى دخل فيه المسبار
And repeat the cauterization until all those corrupted tissues are burned, once or twice or thrice, according to your need.
And beware of burning a nerve, if there is one there, or a large vein.
And if the fistula leads to the body of the bladder or to the body of the intestine, then beware of all these places.
And you only do that if the fistula is in a fleshy place and you estimate that it is not perforated.
Then treat the area until it heals.
If the area seals and the discharge stops from it and remains so for a while, then know that it has completely healed.
And if the discharge does not stop from it, then know that it is perforated or there is a corrupted bone in its depth, or something similar to that, which will be mentioned in its place.

Chapter forty on cauterizing hip dislocation.
Erroneous/Harmful humors may flow to the hip joint, causing it to be dislocated.

If this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize it three times with the large olive-shaped cautery.

Chapter forty-one on cauterizing the sciatic nerve.
If pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and humidity, and you have treated the patient with what we mentioned in the division, but the treatment was not successful, and this becomes chronic, then it is necessary to purge the patient of thick humors with habb al-muntin (asafoetida) or habb al-sabari (aloe vera) and the like. ثمّ اكوه
And the method of cauterization in it is of two types. إمّا كىّ بالأدوية المحرقة وإمّا كىّ بالنار
And cauterization with fire is of many types.
One of them is that you cauterize on the hip joint itself three triangular cauterizations in this manner: وتصير لها عمقا صالحا ويكون بعد ما بين كلّ كيّة وكيّة على قدر غلظ الأصبع وتكون المكواة زيتونيّة
A cauterization may also be performed in the middle, on the head of the hip itself, making four cauterizations.
And if you wish, cauterize it with the circle that was previously mentioned in the cauterization of hip dislocation, a single cauterization, so that the circle surrounds the entire hip and burns the entire thickness of the skin.
This is the method of cauterization for sciatica if the pain is confined to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, cauterize it with two cauterizations on the thigh, on the location where the patient indicates the pain, and one cauterization above the ankle by four fingers, slightly to the lateral side, and the cautery iron should be knife-shaped, and the depth of the cauterization should be only the thickness of the skin.
And if he indicates that the pain extends towards the toes, cauterize it where he indicates, with the point cautery, three or four times, or more if needed.
And if he indicates pain below the knee towards the leg, cauterize there with a single knife-shaped cauterization.
And be careful in all your cauterizations not to reach the point of burning a nerve or a major artery, thus causing the patient a serious injury or chronic illness.
I have seen one and another of those who were cauterized above the ankle, and the cauterization was excessive, so the leg became infected until the infection reached the foot, and it became perforated entirely, and the entire leg was ruined, then diarrhea occurred, and death followed.
If the pain is in both sides, cauterize them both in this same manner.
Some learned physicians have mentioned a cauterization for the hip, whose description is as follows: A cup-like object is made of iron, its diameter being half a span, and at its mouth it is about the thickness of a date pit or slightly less, and inside that cup is another cup, and a third cup, and the distance between each two cups is about the length of a thumb joint, and the cups are open on both sides, and their height is about one or two thumb joints, and a handle of iron is made for them, firmly attached to the cups, and this is its image:
Then it is heated in the fire until it becomes red and throws off sparks. ثمّ توضع على حقّ الورك والعليل متّكئ على الجانب الصحيح
Then leave him for three days and dress it with ghee. وتترك الجرح مفتوحا أيّاما كثيرة
The author of this book said: This type of cauterization we rarely use because of its ugliness and the dreadfulness of its appearance.
And because of the scarcity of those we find who can bear it, except that it is a good cauterization for those who endure it and its proper place is affected.
As for cauterization with burning medications, it is that you make two cups, similar to the rings into which the bolt of the door descends, of copper or iron.
Let there be on their edge a height of about two knuckles or so. ويكون بعد ما بينهما قدر غلظ الأصبع
Then you apply it directly to the hip, with the patient lying on his unaffected side, and you clench your hand well. Then you pour between the two circles some of the corrosive water, which has been slightly warmed by the fire, and you hold it there for the duration of an hourglass. The patient should endure its stinging and burning, for he will feel a burning like fire until the stinging subsides. Then you lift your hand with the instrument and wipe the corrosive water from the entire hip with fresh water. Then you leave it for three days and apply ghee to it until the blackness of the burn disappears. And you leave it for some days while pus flows from it, for this is most effective for the benefit. Then you treat it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the thigh or the leg, you make a mold for it to hold the water, just as you did with the hip.
And this is the description of the corrosive water, which I have already recorded in the treatise on the Rectification of Medicines. تأخذ من ملح القلى ومن الجير غير مطفأ من كلّ واحد جزءا فتسحقهما وتضعهما فى قدر جديدة قد ثقبت أسفلها ثقبة واحدة صغيرة على قدر ما يدخلها المرود وتضع تحت قاع القدر قدرا أخرى مزجّجة وتلقى على القلى والجير من الماء العذب ما يغمرهما بأصبع بعد أن تزمّهما بيدك زمّا جيّدا وتترك القدر حتّى ينزل الماء الحادّ فى أسفل القدر المزحّجة ثمّ تجمع ذلك الماء كلّه ثمّ تلقيه على جير آخر وقلى آخر مجدّدين ايضا فإنّه يكون حينئذ قوىّ الحدّة جدّا يتصرّف فى كثير من أعمال الطبّ وفى كىّ سائر الأعضاء لأنّه يفعل فعل النار بعينها،
Among the medications that can also be used to cauterize the hip are thapsia, honey of jujube, and lime with soap, ground together.
Galen related a story from an ancient man about a treatment for hip pain and sciatica, and he greatly praised it, claiming that no other treatment was needed and that it heals in one go. He even said that sometimes the person entered the bath carried and came out cured. The treatment is that green spurge is taken, and if green is not available, then recently dried spurge is taken. It is finely ground with some fat and placed on the hip where the pain is, or on the leg, or on the thigh. It is bandaged and left for about three hours, or until the patient feels the burning sensation subside. Then he is taken to the bath, and when his body sweats, he is put in the basin. The pain will go away, and he will be cured, God willing.
If he is not cured, then repeat the poultice after ten days, and he will be cured, God willing.
Know that cauterization with these medicines should not be used except after purging the body.
Dioscorides mentioned that goat dung, if used for cauterization of sciatica, is beneficial for it, and the cauterization is done in the following manner.
Wool is taken and soaked in old oil and placed on the deep spot between the thumb and the forearm, closer to the forearm. Then take dry goat dung and ignite it with fire until it becomes an ember. Then place it on the wool and leave it until it is extinguished. Then take another piece. You continue doing this until the sensation reaches the hip through the upper arm, and the pain subsides, God willing. This type of cauterization is called dung cauterization.
The forty-second chapter on cauterizing back pain.
Pain may occur in the back from many causes, either from a fall, a blow, excessive vomiting, or the like.
And it happens from the outpouring of a cold, moist humor.
And cauterization is only applied in this category alone, which results from the outpouring of a cold humor.
Therefore, it is necessary, after the patient vomits with حبّ المنتن (habb al-muntin) or similar, to cauterize his back where the pain is, in three rows across the width of the table itself, after marking the place with ink, in each row five cauterizations or more, according to what you see of the patient's tolerance and strength.
And the cauterization should be with a point cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize him three or four cauterizations with a medium nail-shaped cautery, in this manner:
The thirty-third chapter on cauterizing the beginning of humpbackedness.
This ailment frequently affects young children.
And the sign of its beginning in the child is that he experiences shortness of breath upon standing and moving. وتجد فى آخِر فقارات ظهره خرزة قد برزت تنتو على سائر الخرزات
So if you see that and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery iron that is circular in this way: لتأخذ الكيّة على كلّ جهة من الفقارة باستواء
And if you wish, cauterize it around the vertebra with the point cautery, two or three rows. ولتكن النقط قريبة بعضها من بعض
Then treat the area until it heals with what we have mentioned.
And be careful to use the cautery in the hump that results from a spasm of the nerve.
Chapter forty-four on cauterizing gout and joint pains.
If joint pains are due to cold humors flowing to any part of the body فإذا حدثت الأوجاع فى الرجلين فمن عادة الأطبّاء أن يسمّوا ذلك نقرسا خاصّة
So if cold-caused gout is treated with the types of treatment that we mentioned in the classification and the pains do not go away, then cauterization will remove them.
And that is to cauterize it after emptying (purgation) around the joint of the legs with many cauterizations.

And if you need to cauterize the face of the man, do it with the cautery iron for spotting. فإن صعدت الأوجاع الى الركبتين او الى سائر المفاصل وكثيرا ما يعرض ذلك فاكوه على كلّ ركبة ثلاث كيّات او اربعا من كلّ جهة بهذه المكواة الزيتونيّة بعينها
If you need more than this cauterization, cauterize him, but do not deepen your hand with the cautery, but let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If the pains rise to the hips or to the back, use what we mentioned of cauterization in its chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, cauterize around the two forearms as you go around two rows.
If the pains remain in the fingers, cauterize them on each knuckle a spot and on the back of the hand.
If the pains rise after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize them on each side.
And the sick person should not be without good management and taking medications, for if he improves his diet and vomits the phlegm, he will recover with this cauterization, God willing.
Chapter forty-five on cauterizing hernias.
If a hernia appears in the groin and some of the intestines and omentum descend to the testicle, and this is recent and new, فينبغى أن تأمر العليل بترك الأكل يومه وأن يستعمل من المليّنات ما يحدر به البراز عن جوفه
Then he should lie down on his back in front of you and you order him to hold his breath until the omentum or intestines protrude. ثم تردّه بأصبعك
Then you mark with ink under the hernia on the pubic bone a mark resembling a half-circle, its ends towards the upper part of the body.
Then you heat a cautery, its shape being this:
Until it becomes white and emits sparks. ثمّ تردّ المعاء او الثرب الى جوفه
And the patient's legs have been spread apart, and a pillow has been placed under him. وخادم آخر يعقد على ساقيه وآخر على صدره يمسك يديه
Then apply the cautery iron to the mark itself. ويدك بالمكواة واقفة مستقيمة وتمسكها حتّى تبلغ بها العظم
And be very careful of the protrusion of the intestine while cauterizing, so that you do not burn it, which would cause the patient either death or a great affliction.
And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work will not succeed.
And the cautery iron for children should be gentle, according to their size, and for adults according to their size.
Then treat the cauterized area after three days with ghee until the char of the fire disappears.
Then treat it with other ointments until it heals.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary to make his food, for the duration of his treatment, something that softens his stomach so that the intestine does not protrude during straining and defecation.
Then, if he wants to get up after the forty days, use a tight bandage and keep it on for another forty days.
And reduce exertion, and fullness from food and drink, and loud shouting.
For if he follows this regimen in this way, he will be completely healed, God willing.
And I will mention the treatment of hernias by incision in its chapter, God willing.
As for the hernia that occurs in the rest of the abdomen and is in its early stages, if you want it not to increase, cauterize the hernia with a circular cautery according to its size. وليكن ما تحرق من الجلد مثل ثلثيه
And some of the predecessors have mentioned cauterizing the hernia with a triangular cautery iron in this manner:
After you have marked the hernia with ink, وتصير الخطّ الذى بالعرض فى الجانب الأعلى من الفتق والخطّ الآخر الى اسفل
and the first cauterization is easier and better, God willing.
Chapter forty-six on cauterizing the uvula.
If pain occurs in some organs due to a fall or a blow, and that pain lasts for a long time, and treatment with medications is not effective
then it should be cauterized with a point cautery, and the cauterization of each organ should be according to its size, smallness, weakness, strength, and the severity and chronicity of the pain.
If it heals from the first cauterization, then fine, otherwise, repeat the cauterization because it is the nature of these pains to move from the organ to what is near it. فينبغى أن تتبعها بالكّى حتّى يبرأ العليل
Chapter forty-seven on cauterizing leprosy.
As for those afflicted with leprosy, they may benefit greatly from cauterization, especially a certain type. الجذام الذى يكون من قبل تعفّن البلغم والسوداء
So if you want to cauterize it, examine it; if the leprosy is in its early stages, and you have treated it with what we mentioned in the section on classification, and it has not worsened or stopped, and you fear that the corruption will take over the patient's entire temperament, then cauterize him on the head with five burns: one in the customary center of the head, the second below it towards the forehead at the hairline, two on the temples, and one from behind on the hollow of the nape of the neck. Press your hand firmly with the cautery a little until it affects the bone slightly, and scales come off it, to facilitate the exhalation of the thick vapors from it. And also cauterize him on the spleen itself, as mentioned before.
But if the leprosy has persisted in the patient and has manifested clearly, then it is advisable to cauterize him with these burns that we mentioned on the head, a burn on the tip of the nose, two burns on the cheeks, two burns on the cervical vertebrae, six on the vertebrae of the back, one large one on the coccyx at the base of the tailbone, another above it on the same area, two on the hips, one on each hip, two on the knees, one on each knee, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the nipples of the chest. And cauterize him on every joint of the fingers of his hands and feet with a burn, and on each heel of his feet and ulna of his hands, and be careful of the nerve that is on the back of the heels, lest you burn them.
He may also be cauterized with a burn on the pubic bone, another on the cardia of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you cauterize, the more beneficial and effective it is.
And know that the sick person does not feel pain from cauterization as a healthy person does, because his body is numb.
The cauteries should be of a size appropriate for the organs and joints, according to the descriptions of the irons that have been given.
Then treat the cauterization with powdered chickpea flour mixed with honey and other treatments until he recovers, God willing.
Chapter forty-eight on cauterizing numbness.
When a limb is numb and is treated with medications, ointments, and bandages, but does not heal فاكو نفس العضو المنخدر بكيّات على حسب ما يستحقّ عظم العضو او صغره
And let your cauterization penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin. ثمّ تعالجه بالمرهم حتّى يبرأ
And some numbness that affects the hand and foot may be cauterized in the vertebrae of the back at the exit of the nerve that moves that limb, so the numbness goes away.
And no one should undertake this except someone who is knowledgeable about the anatomy of the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
Chapter forty-nine on cauterizing vitiligo.
If vitiligo becomes chronic and no medical remedy works for it فأكو عليه كيّا فيه عمق قليلا على قدر ثخن الجلد
then treat it with lentil flour, rose oil, plantain leaves, and pigeon blood or swallow blood, one part of each ويخلط الجميع ويطلى على خرقة ويلزم الموضع حتّى يبرأ
Chapter fifty on cauterizing cancer.
If the cancer is in its early stages and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a circular cautery iron around it as it rotates.
Some physicians have mentioned that it should be cauterized with a deep cautery in its center, but I do not see that because I expect it to ulcerate. وقد شاهدت ذلك مرّات
So the correct way is to cauterize around it in a circle as we said, or with many cauterizations.
Chapter fifty-one on cauterizing the furuncle.
If a furuncle occurs in someone and it is slow to ripen, either because of the agent causing it, or because of the age of the patient if he is old and has little blood, or because of the time, وأردت أن تسرع فى نضج الدبيلة فاكو حواليها بكيّات صغار كثيرة تنقيطا
If you want to treat it with cauterization, then heat the iron which has this shape:
And insert it in the middle of the furuncle until it penetrates the skin.
And let the cautery be from what is below so that the flow of pus is facilitated.
Then treat it with what is necessary until it heals.
Chapter fifty-two on cauterizing the corroding ulcer.
The corroding ulcer is but a corruption that spreads in the organ, consuming it as fire consumes dry wood.
If you see the corroding ulcer in a place that can tolerate cauterization with fire, heat many nail-shaped cauteries, small and large, according to what is suitable for the place where the corroding ulcer is.
Then cauterize it from every side until all the corruption is eradicated and nothing of it remains at all.
Then leave it for three days and apply powdered sulfur with oil to the cauterized areas until all the scab and all the corruption is removed.
Then treat it with ointments that promote flesh growth.
If, after three days, you see that the flesh is growing healthily without corruption, then [it is fine]; otherwise, repeat the cauterization on the remaining corrupted areas.
The corroding ulcer can also be treated with a potent medication, as it acts as a quicker substitute for fire.
I have mentioned its treatment with the potent medication in the classification, so take it from there whenever you need it.
Chapter fifty-three on cauterizing inverted and non-inverted nails.
This ailment frequently occurs on the soles of the feet, and it is a rough thing that pains the man.
Cauterization for it is of two types: either cauterization by fire or cauterization by strong water.
As for cauterization by fire, it is that you heat the hollow iron, similar to an eagle's feather, made of iron to the extent that it surrounds the nail on all sides, and it has a thin edge, then you place it hot on the nail, then you rotate your hand with the iron around the nail until the iron reaches the depth of the nail, and you leave it for three days while it suppurates, then you dress it with wild mallow pounded with salt, and you leave the dressing on it for a night, then it will be uprooted, then you treat the site of the wound with the ointment that generates flesh until it heals.
If the nails are not inverted, and they frequently occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet, then you should take a tube of copper or of iron or of eagle's feather, and place it on the nail or wart, then you pour into the tube a small amount of strong water, and you hold your hand while rotating it with a slight pinch of your hand so that the edge of the tube affects the base of the nail, and the strong water finds a way to penetrate to the base of the nail, and the patient bears the sting of the strong water for a short time, then you leave it, then the nail will be uprooted.
Thus, you do to them one by one until you have treated all of them in the body, then you treat their places after they are uprooted with what generates flesh from ointments.
Chapter fifty-four on cauterizing tremors.
If someone experiences tremors due to coldness in the nerves or from quartan fever or other causes فينبغى أن تكويه أربع كيّات او خمسا على خرز الظهر بين كلّ خرزة كيّة
for the tremors will cease and it accelerates the maturation of the cold illness.
Chapter fifty-five on cauterizing pustules occurring on the body.
Ugly pustules may erupt on the body, arising from cold, thick, and corrupt humors.
Therefore, upon their first appearance, it is necessary to cauterize the head of each pustule gently with an aloeswood stick, the tip of which has been ignited by fire, or with the root of long birthwort, or with a lentil-shaped cautery iron.
Carbuncles may also be cauterized in the same manner upon their first appearance, so that they do not increase, and the causative excess dissipates, and the patient recovers.
However, it is necessary that this be done after the patient has been evacuated by bloodletting.
Chapter fifty-six on cauterizing bleeding occurring when an artery is severed.
Bleeding often occurs from an artery that has been severed during an external wound, or when incising a tumor, or cauterizing an organ, and so on, making it difficult to stop.
So if this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger over the opening of the artery and press firmly until the blood is trapped beneath your finger and nothing comes out.
Then place several small and large olive-shaped cauteries in the fire and blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one of them, either small or large depending on the wound and the place where the artery ruptured, and apply the cautery to the vessel itself after quickly removing your finger, holding the cautery until the bleeding stops.
If the blood gushes out when you lift your finger from the opening of the artery and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another cautery from those prepared in the fire, and continue doing this one after another until the bleeding stops, taking care not to burn a nerve that might be there, thus causing the patient further harm.
Know that if an artery bleeds, it cannot be stopped, especially if it is a large artery, except by one of four methods: either by cauterization as we have said, or by severing it if it has not already been severed, for if it is severed, its ends will contract and the bleeding will stop, or by tying it tightly with threads, or by applying medications that stop bleeding and applying tight bandages.
As for those who try to stop it with a bandage, or by tightening it with rags, or by applying burning substances, and so on, it will not stop at all by that, except rarely.
If this happens to someone and there is no doctor or medicine present, he should immediately place his index finger over the opening of the wound itself, as we have described, and press very firmly until the blood is contained and comes out from above the wound, and he should continually apply very cold water to the artery and finger, without removing it, until the blood clots, thickens, and stops flowing.
Meanwhile, consider what cauterization or medication he needs.
The second chapter on incision, lancing, phlebotomy, wounds, and the like.
Khalaf said: We have mentioned in the first chapter every disease suitable for cauterization with fire and burning medicine, its causes and reasons, its instruments, and forms of cauteries, and I have made that into chapters from the head to the foot.
And I follow in this chapter the same path to make it easy for the student to obtain what he seeks.
And before I begin with that, it is necessary for you to know, my sons, that this chapter contains more danger than the first chapter on cauterization, and for that reason, the warning in it should be stronger, because the work in this chapter often involves the discharge of blood, by which life is sustained, when opening a vein, or incising a swelling, or lancing an abscess, or treating a wound, or extracting an arrow, or incising a stone, and similar things, all of which are accompanied by danger and fear, and in most of them, death occurs.
And I advise you against falling into what is doubtful for you, for various types of people may come to you in this profession with various kinds of illnesses, and among them are those who have become weary of their illness, and death has become insignificant to them due to the intensity of their suffering and the length of their affliction, and the illness has reached a stage that indicates death.
And among them are those who offer you their wealth and enrich you with it, hoping for health, but their illness is fatal, so it is not appropriate for you to help anyone who comes to you with such a condition at all, and let your caution be stronger than your desire and eagerness, and do not proceed with anything of that until after certain knowledge is established with you regarding the good outcome it will lead to.
And use in all the treatment of your patients the precedence of knowledge and warning about what the safety will lead to, for in that, you will have help in acquiring praise, glory, remembrance, and thanks.
May God inspire you, my sons, with His guidance, and may He not deprive you of correctness and success. Indeed, that is in His hand, there is no god but Him.
And I have arranged this chapter into sections, as presented in the chapter on cauterization, from the head to the foot, to make it easier for you to obtain what you want from it, God willing.
The first chapter on the treatment of water that collects in the heads of children.
This ailment often occurs to boys at birth if the midwife squeezes the boy's head without gentleness.
It may also occur from a hidden cause that is not known.
And I have not seen this ailment in anyone other than boys. وجميع من رأيت منهم أسرع اليه الموت
And I have certainly seen among them a boy whose head was filled with water, and the head grew larger every day until the boy could not sit up on his own due to the size of his head. والرطوبة تتزايد حتّى هلك
And this moisture either gathers between the skin and the bone, or it gathers beneath the bone on the periosteum.
And the treatment for that, if the moisture is between the skin and the bone and the swelling is small, it is necessary to make one horizontal incision in the middle of the head, and the length of the incision should be about two knuckles so that the moisture flows out.
And this is a picture of the lancet.
If the moisture is greater and the swelling is larger, then make it two intersecting incisions in this way:
And if the moisture is under the bone وعلامته أن ترى خياطات الرأس مفتوحة من كلّ جهة
And after the incision, all the moisture comes out. ثمّ تشدّ الشقوق بالخرق والرفائد
Then the bandage is loosened, and the wound is treated with bandages and ointments.
And do not neglect to tighten the head moderately. وتغذّى العليل بكلّ غذاء جافّ قليل الرطوبة الى أن يقوى العضو ويبرأ
Another method of incision is to look where the bone of the swelling and the accumulation of water appear.
Because it may be more in the back of the head or in the front of it, or on the right or on the left.
So you aim the incision where the swelling and the fullness of water appeared to you. فتشقّه على ما يمكنك
And be careful not to cut an artery, causing bleeding, so that the patient dies from that bleeding with the discharge of moisture.
The second chapter on cutting the two arteries that are behind the ears, known as the throbbing arteries.
When someone experiences acute episodes affecting the eyes or chest, and this becomes chronic, and medication does not work, then the most effective treatment is to cut these two arteries.
Therefore, if you intend to cut them, you should shave the patient's head with a razor, then rub the area with a rough cloth so that the artery appears, then tie the patient's neck with the excess of his garment, then look where the vein pulsates, and their locations are the two lowered places behind the ears, and they are rarely hidden except in some people, then mark them with ink, then cut them with a sharp scalpel down to the bone, and this should be across the width of the head.
And if you wish, you can insert the scalpel from under the artery and lift it upwards while cutting, and the length of the cut should be about two closed fingers, because when the vein is cut, the blood will come out in a pulsating flow, leaping forward in successive spurts.
If the artery is not apparent to the touch, then you should measure from the ear a distance of about three fingers, then mark it with ink and incise down to the bone.
It is advisable to let out six ounces of blood on average, and sometimes you may let out more or less, all depending on the patient's strength and the fullness of his arteries as it appears to you.
Then look at the wound, and if any membrane remains on the bone, cut it so that a hot swelling does not occur, then tie the wound with a wick of linen cloth, then treat it with ointments until it heals.
The third chapter on the consumption/inflammation of the two arteries which are in the temples.
If a person experiences chronic migraine or acute catarrh due to sharp humors and heat in the muscles of the temples, or severe chronic headache and the like, and is treated with various medical treatments, but that does not work فقد جرّبنا فى هذه الأمراض سلّ الشريانات من الأصداغ او كيّها كما وصفنا
And the way to incise them is that the patient shaves the hair that is on the temples وتقصد الشريان الظاهر فى الصدغ فإنّه يتبيّن لك من نبضه
If it is hidden from you, then let the patient tighten his neck with the extra part of his garment. ثمّ تحكّ أنت الموضع بخرقة او تكمّد الموضع بماء حارّ حتّى يظهر الشريان ظهورا بيّنا واضحا
If the artery is thin, twist it with the tip of the hook. ثمّ تقطع منه جزءا على قدر ما يتباعد طرفاه وتنقبض ولا تحدث نزفا
Then let out blood from six to three ounces.
If the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong doubled thread. وليكن الخيط إمّا من ابريسم وإما من أوتار العود لئلّا يسرع اليه العفن قبل التحام الجرح فيحدث النزف
Then cut the excess between the two ligatures. تفعل ذلك فى تلك الساعة او بعد وقت آخر
And if you wish, cauterize it to the bone with a knife-shaped cautery until its ends are severed, which will serve the same purpose, or better, as we have said.
Except if the patient has a fever or a hot temperament, because cauterization helps to destroy moisture, so it is more effective in benefit.
It is necessary after severing the arteries to stuff the place with worn cotton and place tight bandages on it.
And after the resolution, treat it with dry medicines that grow flesh and with bandaging until it heals, God willing.
If bleeding from the artery occurs during your work, immediately cut it either by cauterization وإمّا أن تملأ الموضع بالزاج وتشدّ يدك حتّى ينقطع الدم
And what is lighter and easier than severing the artery is to cauterize the vessel with this two-bladed cautery after marking the two places with ink and applying it very hot until it reaches the bone and the vessel is cut in two places so that the space between its ends widens. فإنّه لا يلتحم بهذا الكىّ البتّة
And this is the image of the cautery:
The sharpness of the two knives resembles the two small intestines, except that they are much less sharp than the knife, because if they were as sharp as the knife, the cold would reach them faster and the meat would not be cut quickly.
So if there is some thickness in them, the heat of the fire will be retained in them, and they will cut the meat quickly.
And this method is better than any other method, lighter, and easier.
And let the distance between the two knives be the thickness of a finger.
The fourth chapter on the treatment of the constant flow of hot tears to the eyes.
If the tears are constant and their flow is from the veins that are on the skull from the outside, and there is no benefit from any medical treatment with medicines ورأيت وجه العليل قد احمّر ويحسّ فى جبينه دبيبا كدبيب النمل وعيناه مهزولتان رطبتان قد تأكّلت اشفارهما وتشبّطت اجفانهما من حدّة الدموع
which is that you order the patient to shave the hair that is on his forehead, then you make three parallel incisions in the forehead along the length of the forehead, and the length of the incision should be about two fingers الشقّ الواحد موازيا لطول الأنف فى وسط الجبهة والثانى على البعد قليلا من حركة العضل الذى فى الصدغ والثالث من الجهة الأخرى
and beware of cutting the two arteries that are on the sides, and keep your hand away from the joining of the jaws ويكون بعد كلّ شقّ قدر ثلاث اصابع مضمومة
and let there be with you prepared pieces of sponge or many dry rags with which you dry the blood
then you insert the double-edged scalpel, which is this image of it من الشقّ الذى يلى الصدغ الى الشقّ الأوسط وتسلخ به جميع الجلد الذى فيما بين الشقّين مع الصفاق الذى على العظم
And its sharp side is placed upwards towards the flesh attached to the skin, and its smooth side towards the bone. وتدفعها حتّى تنتهى الى الشقّ الأوسط وتقطع بها جميع الأوعية التى تنزل من الرأس الى العينين من غير أن يصل القطع الى ظاهر الجلد
Then you do the same in the middle incision to the other incision.
And after a moderate amount of blood has flowed, you squeeze the areas of the solidified blood clots.
Then you put a wick of cotton dipped in wine and oil or vinegar and oil in each incision. لئلّا يحدث ورم حارّ
And on the third day you loosen the bandage and use frequent washing with lukewarm water. ثمّ تعالجه بمرهم الباسليقون بدهن الورد وسائر ما تعالج به الجراحات الى أن يبرأ إن شاء الله
The fifth chapter on the treatment of tears and discharges to the eyes from inside the head.
When someone experiences numerous, severe, sharp, and persistent episodes of nasal discharge, and their eyes appear sunken and small, with weakened vision, ulcerated eyelids, and loss of eyelashes, accompanied by a sharp, painful headache deep within the head and continuous sneezing, فاعلم من هذه الأعراض أنّ تلك الموادّ والنزلات إنّما تجىء من عروق كثيرة عميقة وأفضل العلاج فيها هذا العلاج،
Order the patient to shave their forehead, then make a single incision in the middle of the forehead, or slightly higher horizontally, starting the incision from the left temple to the right temple, reaching the bone. Keep your hand away from the temple muscles that move during chewing until the bone is exposed. Dry all the blood with a sponge, then separate the edges of the incision with worn cotton or a twisted piece of linen. Then bandage it from above with compresses soaked in wine and oil to prevent the formation of a hot swelling.
When you remove the bandage and see that the hot swelling has subsided, you should scrape the bone until the flesh begins to grow. Then treat it with a drying remedy that promotes flesh growth, such as taking two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, preparing an ointment from them, and using it for flesh growth in such wounds.
The sixth chapter on the treatment of what falls into the ear.
Everything that falls into the ear is one of four types: either a mineral stone or something like stone, such as iron and glass; or a plant seed, such as chickpeas and kernels, and so on; or a flowing thing, such as water and vinegar, and so on; or an animal.
When a pebble or something like a pebble, which does not grow in the ear, falls into the ear, face the ear towards the sun. If you see the pebble, drop in it a bit of violet oil or candle wax, then try to remove it by moving the head or by sneezing with hellebore, blocking the nostrils when the sneeze comes, after placing a ring of rags or wool around the ear and pulling the ear upwards; often it comes out with this treatment.
If it doesn't come out, then try to remove it with the gentle instrument which is pictured here:
If it comes out with the husk, fine, otherwise try to extract it with a smooth, blunt hook with little curvature.
If it doesn't come out with that, then make a tube of copper and insert the end of the tube gently into the ear hole. وسدّ ما حوالى الأنبوبة بالقير المليّن بالدهن لئلّا يكون للريح طريق غير الأنبوبة
If it doesn't come out with what we described, then take a small amount of gum arabic or processed gum, which is used for catching birds. فضعه فى طرف المرود بعد أن تلفّ عليه قطنة محكمة
If it doesn't come out with all that we described, then proceed to incision before a hot swelling occurs or it becomes tense.
The method of incision is to first phlebotomize the patient in the cephalic vein and draw blood according to his strength. ثمّ تجلس العليل بين يديك وتقلب أذنه الى فوق وتشقّ شقّا صغيرا فى أصل الأذن عند شحمته فى الموضع المنخفض منها
Then stitch the incision immediately quickly and treat it until it heals.
But if the thing that has fallen into the ear is one of the grains that swell and expand, try to extract it with what we mentioned.
If it doesn't come out, then take a thin, delicate scalpel like this: وحاول به قطع ذلك النوع من الحبوب الساقطة فى الأذن
And you only do that if you are certain that that grain has been moistened by the ear’s vapor until it becomes many small pieces.
Then you extract it with the blind hook, or with soft date fibers, or by sucking, as we mentioned. فإنّه يسهل إخراجها
As for water that has entered the ear, the patient should first use sneezing with hellebore. وقد ملأ أذنه بشىء من القطن البالى وهو مضطجع على تلك الأذن التى فيها الماء
If it comes out with that, fine; otherwise, take many pebbles the length of fingers, thin and smooth. فتدفّئها بالنار قليلا
The water may also come out by taking one papyrus reed or feather. ويدخل طرفها الواحد فى الأذن
Or you can draw it out with the tube in the way that was described with the pebble.
As for removing an animal that has entered the ear, observe: if it is small-bodied like a flea or similar, treat it with what I mentioned in the section.
But if its body is large, perceptible to the senses, try to extract it with date fibers and hooks. وأمره أسهل من جميع ما ينشب فى الأذن
As for removing worms that have developed in the ear, if you treated it with what we mentioned in the section on ear drops and your treatment was not successful, فينبغى أن تنظر الى الأذن فى الشمس فإن ظهر اليك شىء من الدود فأخرجه بالجفت او بالصنانير اللطاف
If none appear to you, then take a tube; this is its form: ضيقة الأسفل واسعة الأعلى
If it doesn't come out, seal around the tube with wax as I mentioned to you regarding the stone.
If it doesn't come out with what we mentioned, use the ear drops that I mentioned. وقد جرّبتها الأوائل فى قتل الدود
And your pouring of oils and medicines into the ear will be with this instrument. وهده صورتها:
And if you wish, the nozzle that is inside the tube can be made of well-wrought copper. وإن شئت أخذت مرودا ولففت فى طرفه قطنة لفّا محكما ثمّ تلقى الدهن او العصارة او ما تريد من هذه الأدوية فى الأنبوبة وهى فى الأذن ثمّ تدخل المرود بالقطنة من فوق وتعصر به يدك عصرا معتدلا حتّى يندفع الدهن فى جوف السمع ويحسّ به العليل داخلا.
