And let what you pour into the ear be slightly warmed by the fire. واحذر ن يكون الشىء الذى يقطّر فيها باردا جدّا او حارّا جدّا فإنّ الأذن لا تحتمل ذلك،
Chapter seven on the treatment of sudden blockage of the ear.
Some children may come out of their mothers' wombs with the pores of their ears not perforated.
Also, some people may experience a blockage in the ear canal due to an injury or flesh growing in it.
This blockage may be in the depth of the ear hole, imperceptible to sight. وقد يعرض الى خارج الثقب قليلا ويدركه البصر.
So the one that appears in the depth of the ear and is not perceptible to sight is, in most cases, difficult to see.
And the one that is perceptible to sight, you should place the patient's ear in the sun and look into it. فإن رأيت السدّ ظاهرا فافتحه بمبضع لطيف تكون هذه صورته:
Its tip should have some slight, limited width, and the rest of the scalpel should be smooth on both sides so as not to injure the ear.
If the blockage is due to flesh that has grown in the ear canal, grasp it with delicate forceps and cut it very gently until all the flesh is extracted.
If the blockage is deep in the ear, take a smooth, delicate probe, warm it slightly in the fire, then insert it into the ear canal. If you feel the blockage, along with the patient's experience of hearing difficulty, rub it gently with the probe, being careful not to injure the eardrum. Then, place a wick in the ear, sized according to the width of the opening, having coated it in Egyptian ointment. Do this for several days until you are sure the wound will not close up.
Or, take a wick, moisten it in water, sprinkle powdered vitriol on it, and use it.
If you see that the ear has become swollen with a hot swelling, it is necessary to remove the wick and replace it with another wick that you have coated in a cerate made with rose oil until the hot swelling subsides, then continue treating it until it heals.
If bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge or cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use the rest of the treatment that stops bleeding, as mentioned in the chapter on ear drops.
The eighth chapter on the treatment of warts that appear on the eyelids.
These warts that appear on the eyelids may be moist and may be dry.
It is necessary to grasp them with tweezers or a hook and cut them with a scalpel from their roots. ثّم تحمل على الموضع زاجا مسحوقا،
If it bleeds, cauterize it with a gentle lenticular cautery iron.
And cauterizing it is better after cutting. وكثيرا ما تعود اذا بقى من أصولها شىء.
Chapter nine on the treatment of the cold affecting the eyelids.
Often, something appears in the eyelids that resembles hail in its intensity and hardness, and therefore it is called hail.
It is a collection of thick moisture in the upper eyelid and the lower eyelid.
The procedure for it is that you look, and if the hailstone is prominent on the outer surface of the eyelid, moving in every direction, then its treatment is easy.
Make a horizontal incision on it, then gently peel it from each side until it is freed, then hook it with a fishhook and cut it off.
And if you are unable to cut it off unless after piercing through the eyelid with the cut, it will not harm the patient at all.
If the incision is large, then close it with stitches and treat it until it heals.
And if it is small, there is no harm in it for you, because the ointment will strengthen it and heal it.
If the hailstone is tilted towards the inside of the eyelid, towards the inner surface, then turn the eyelid over and hook the hailstone with a fishhook without needing an incision, and cut it off from each side.
If it pierces through the eyelid with the cut, it will not harm at all.
Then, after cutting off the hailstone, wash the eye with salt water and treat the area with something that heals until the patient recovers.
The tenth chapter on the treatment of sharanaq that appears in the eyelid.
A sharnaq is a small lump that forms in the layers of the upper eyelid, and it occurs most often in children, making their eyes heavy and causing them to experience colds in the early mornings.
They are unable to look at sunlight because tears quickly come to their eyes, and so you see them constantly leaning on their faces, and they sleep on them, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are moist, swollen, and the protrusion of the sharnaq is visible. ومتى كبّست الموضع بأصابعك أحسست بالشرناق بينهما.
The procedure is to place the patient's head in your lap, then take a linen cloth, prepare a wick from it, and make a circle from that wick to the extent that it surrounds the sharnaq from all sides, then place it on it and press with your fingers from all sides to gather the sharnaq in the center of the circle, then make a horizontal incision in the middle of that moist area with a lancet, and the incision should not be larger than the incision made for bloodletting.
As for the depth, you should incise the entire skin until you reach the sharnaq, and in most cases the sharnaq will protrude from the incision in the form of a white piece of fat, so pull it out with a cloth that you have wrapped between your fingers while turning your hand right and left until it is completely removed.
Beware of increasing the size of the incision, lest the lancet reach the eye and harm it.
If the sharnaq does not appear to you at the beginning of the incision, then you should increase the incision slightly and gently until the sharnaq appears, then pull it out as we mentioned.
Then dip a cloth in vinegar and water and place it on the area and bandage it with a soft dressing.
Some people crush salt and place it in the cavity of the incision to dissolve what remains of that moisture, then treat it until it heals.
If a hot swelling occurs in the area, treat it with soothing compresses until it heals.
Chapter eleven on the types of twitching of the eye.
If extra eyelashes grow on the eyelid in an unnatural way under the natural eyelashes and persist, they harm the eye and cause various diseases such as constant tearing, relaxation of the eyelids, whiteness, and thickness, until this becomes a cause of blindness.
Lifting the eye has four aspects: either by cauterization with fire, or with a sharp medicine as mentioned in the chapter on cauterization. وإمّا أن يكون التشمير بالقطع والخياطة او بالقصب على ما أنا ذاكره
You should put the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid with your left hand; if it turns over, then fine, otherwise insert a needle with a thread from the bottom of the eyelid and pass the needle with the thread from above, and this should be near the hair itself, and pull the thread up with the eyelid and turn it over with the probe, then make an incision inside the eyelid below the extra hair with the lancet, from the larger corner to the smaller corner, then remove the thread and place a small pad of cotton or cloth under the eyelid, then mark on the eyelid with ink a shape like a myrtle leaf, except that the shape should be as much as you want to lift the eyelid, because people may differ in this; some need to cut from the eyelid a suitable amount according to how much the eyelid has relaxed, and some need to cut less; all of this depends on the degree of relaxation of the eyelid.
Then you make an incision with the scalpel on the two lines that you marked, and start from the larger corner to the smaller corner, and one incision should be near the natural hair, about the thickness of the probe, then insert the hook into one of the corners of the skin, then peel it all off, then join the two edges by stitching with a needle and thin wool thread, and wipe the blood and stick the remaining threads on the eyebrows with some sticky substance if you want to do that, otherwise it doesn't matter.
Then leave the stitching and the threads for about three or four days, then treat it.
If you wish, you can leave the wound without stitching and treat it with something that dries and constricts, for the eyelid will rise when the wound closes and joins, and stitching is better.
This method of lifting was mentioned by the ancients, but it is a burden on the patient, although it is good work and there is no danger in it.
And another method of lifting is to mark a shape on the eyelid like the shape of a myrtle leaf as we described, then lift the eyelid with three hooks that are either separate or joined in this way.
Then you cut what remains of the eyelid with small scissors in this manner, cutting moderately.
If you cannot restrain the quivering and it does not settle for you, take a needle with thread in it and insert it in the middle of the figure, insert another thread near the larger corner, and a third thread near the smaller corner, and gather the threads between your fingers evenly, then raise your hand with it moderately and lift the marked skin entirely as we have described.
Then bring the edges of the wound together by stitching and treat it until it heals; if a hot swelling appears at your cutting or incision, soothe that swelling with qayruti and similar soothing ointments.
It may also happen to the lower eyelid that its lashes turn inward, so it is necessary to use what we have mentioned of cutting, stitching, cauterizing with fire and with a sharp medicine, and cauterizing with fire or with a sharp medicine is more effective and gentler on the patient than cutting and stitching, and cutting and stitching are more effective.
Cauterization with reeds is done in this manner: you turn the eyelid and make the incision from the inside as described, then you make two thin reeds or pieces of wood the length of the eyelid and their width less than the width of a lancet, and notches are carved in their ends on both sides where the threads hold, then you bring them together gently over what remains of the eyelid and tighten the two reeds from both sides tightly and firmly and leave it for days, so the tightened skin dies, blackens, and rots until it falls off by itself, and if it is slow, cut it off with scissors, then treat it until it heals.
When it heals, the eyelid will be raised and the lashes will not prick the eye, and this is the picture of the two reeds, make it in this shape and this size in length and width precisely.
Chapter twelve on lifting the irritating hair from the eye with a needle.
If it is a hair or two, the procedure for that is to take a thin needle and insert in it a smooth, thin silk thread. ثمّ تجمع طرفيه وتعقدهما عقدة لطيفة جدّا
Then attach to the loop another thin thread, shorter than it. واعقد طرفيه إن شئت
Then have the patient place his head in your lap and let it be near the sun so that the work is clear, for it is delicate work.
Then insert the needle with the loop at the base of the extra hair and pass it quickly through the eyelid until you bring it out from above the natural hair.
Then pull the thread over the loop and insert that hair into the loop, whether it is one or two or three, no more.
Then pull it with your hand until the hair comes out with the loop in the eyelid along with the natural hair.
If you pull the loop and the hair does not come out with it, pull the loop down with the thread you attached to it until the loop comes out of the upper hole.
Then put the hair back in it and pull them both. تفعل ذلك حتّى ترتفع فى الثقب الأعلى وتراها رأى العين
Then release the loop and the thread and remove them. وشدّ العين واتركها مشدودة يومين او ثلاثة حتّى تلزم الشعرة مكانها وينبت عليها اللحم
If the hair is short, then either add to it a long hair from the natural hair, so it will rise with it, or leave it until it grows longer after a while, then you can remove it.
Chapter thirteen on the treatment of the fissure that occurs in the upper eyelid.
The eye that is affected by this fissure is called "hare-eye".
And this fissure is either natural or accidental.
The accidental one results from the healing of a wound, a tear, a cauterization, or something similar.
The way to treat it is to incise that healed part and separate its edges and place between them a wick of linen and tie it until it heals.
And it is not appropriate to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict, because if you do that, the fissure will return worse than it was.
Rather, use things that soften, such as fenugreek and poultices with water in which marshmallow and flaxseed have been soaked, and diachylon ointment melted with some oil, and smear the wick with it and treat with it.
And the key to its treatment is to strive by every means that it does not heal in the way it was originally.
And this treatment that we mentioned is only a partial repair of the fissure, not that the appearance of the place returns exactly as it was originally.
Chapter fourteen on the treatment of the fissure that occurs in the lower eyelid.
This fissure that occurs in the lower eyelid is what is truly called a fissure. وتكون طبيعيّة وتكون عرضيّة.
The accidental one results from a wound, a cut, cauterization, and the like.
The way to operate on it is to take a needle with doubled thread and insert it into the flesh, passing it from the left corner to the right corner until the thread is at both edges of the flesh.
Then you stretch the flesh upwards with the needle and cut it with a wide scalpel.
If the shape of the eyelid returns to how it should be, then fine; otherwise, you take a small probe and place it on the location of the fissure and turn the eyelid with it, and you make two incisions on the inner side of the eyelid, with the ends of the two incisions starting from the corners of the cut you made until they meet, forming an angle so that when they join, its shape becomes similar to this shape:
And it is the letter lam in Greek.
Then you remove that flesh as much as the sharp side of it is below what follows the eyelid. ثمّ تجمع الأجزاء المتفرّقة بخياطتين تخيطه بخيط صوف
Then you treat it with what we mentioned of relaxing medicines and twisting until it heals.
And if the eyelid split occurred from an incision or stitching or cauterization, then it is necessary to make a simple incision below the hair of the eyelashes also as mentioned before. ثمّ تفرّق بين الشفتين بفتل على ما ذكرنا
The summary of the treatment of the eyelid split, if it is from above or from below, is that you perform the work according to what is available to you from the form of the eyelid split. فإنّها قد تكون كثيرة الاختلاف فى الصورة
And the experienced craftsman manages the trick in any way possible until he restores the form to its natural state or close to it.
The disease itself will guide you to what is suitable for it in terms of work and instruments in most cases.
The fifteenth chapter is on the adhesion of the eyelid to the conjunctiva or to the cornea.
This adhesion may occur to many people, where the upper eyelid adheres to the white of the eye, preventing it from easy movement and hindering its natural functions.
Therefore, you should insert the tip of a probe under the eyelid and lift it upwards or stretch it with a hook, then cut the adhesion with a gentle scalpel, not as sharp as cutting scalpels, but somewhat blunt, so that the patient does not become anxious during the procedure and the scalpel slips and injures the eye with its sharpness.
And your cutting should be as if you are peeling off that adhesion, and wait until the eyelid returns to its natural state and the entire adhesion heals, then pour salt water into the eye, wash it with it, or instill in it a solution of vitriol suppositories dissolved in water.
Then separate between the eyelid and the eye with a linen wick and place cotton wool soaked in egg white over the eye, and after the third day use desiccating suppositories until it heals.
Chapter Sixteen on cutting the nail and the growth of flesh of the nail beds.
The pterygium is of two types: either nervous, and it resembles a hard, thin membrane. وإمّا أن تكون غير عصبيّة تشبه رطوبة جامدة بيضاء اذا مسّها الحديد او رمت أخذها بالصنّارة تقطّعت ولم تثبت فيها صنّارة.
Both types begin from the greater canthus, and they slowly creep until they cover the pupil and obstruct the light and the movement of the eye.
The method of its removal is that the patient places his head in your lap, then he opens his eyes, and you lift the eyelid with your hand, then you grasp the pterygium with a slightly curved hook and pull it upwards. ثمّ تأخذ إبرة وتدخل فيها شعرة من شعر الخيل او البقر وخيط قوىّ وتثنى طرف الإبرة قليلا وتغرزها فى وسط الظفرة وتنفذها بالإبرة وتربط بالخيط الظفرة وتمدّها الى فوق.
Then you cut the remainder at the base of the canthus with a fine scalpel or small scissors and leave the natural flesh of the canthus, lest constant tearing result from its cutting.
And you may pull the pterygium with the hook alone or with the thread as we have said, then you peel with the smooth scalpel the edge which this is its picture:
And beware that the scalpel touches the cornea, causing a hernia in it, so the pupil swells.
Then, after the incision, put in the eye some powdered salt or some zinc sulfate suppositories and leave it until the next day, then treat it as needed until it heals.
If the pterygium is not fleshy and you are unable to insert a needle in it, nor fix a hook in it, then this type of pterygium is often treated with medications and heals as described in the classification.
And if you want to excise it, open the patient's eye and take a fine, smooth scalpel with a weak edge, in this manner: واجرد الظفرة به من فوق جردا بلطف
Then repeat the procedure until it is all gone. إلّا إن اعترضك فى العين ورم حارّ فاتركها وعالج الورم الحارّ حتّى يبرأ
Then repeat the scraping procedure on it until it heals.
As for a fleshy outgrowth of the conjunctiva, if the outgrowth harms the eye excessively, فعلّق ذلك النتو بالصنّارة واقطع منه بعضه
Then instill into the eyes red collyrium or copper sulfate collyrium until it heals.
Chapter seventeen on cutting the warding and what grows of excess flesh in the eye.
Red, overlapping flesh may grow in the eyes of some people until it covers the pupil, or comes close to it, or overflows onto the eyelids. وربّما انقلبت الأجفان الى خارج ويشبه ورد الجلنار.
The procedure for this is to have the patient place their head in your lap, then open their eyes, and you pick up all of that red flesh with suitable small hooks, or grasp it with tweezers or forceps, then cut the flesh bit by bit until it is all gone by cutting, and be careful of the eye so as not to harm it during the procedure.
Your cutting of it should be either with the scalpel that we described for cutting the pterygium, or with small scissors like those used to pluck hairs, as their image will appear in the chapter following this chapter.
Once your cutting is complete and all the fleshy growth is gone, fill the eye with crushed salt, or drip into it red vitriol and similar corrosive medications, and apply cotton with egg white on the eye from the outside to prevent hot swelling.
If any of the fleshy growth remains and the bleeding overwhelms you, and you fear hot swelling, then leave the eye and treat it with something that soothes the swelling, then return to it with the procedure until it heals.
And likewise do the same with the excess flesh that appears in the eye of this type, except that you should avoid treating any eye that is weak by nature or by accidental cause with iron instruments.
And do not put your hand to any of these procedures until you see that the organ can tolerate that procedure.
Chapter eighteen on dripping eye drops into the eye.
Cobwebs are red veins that are woven over the eye, preventing it from performing its function of sight.
And the eye weakens with the length of days, so it is necessary for you first to look; if the eye in which the cobwebs are is strong and there is no other disease in it other than the cobwebs, then the plucking is that you order the ill person to place his head in your lap, then hang those veins with one hook or two depending on your skill, and the hooks should be smooth in bending according to this picture:
Or it may be two double hooks in one body, in this form:
Then you gently pick up those veins with fine scissors and gently wipe away the blood from time to time until you see that those veins have disappeared from the eye and the blood has been drained.
And be careful with the eye, do not hurt it with the tips of the scissors.
And let your work be at midday, facing the sun. وتثبت فى عملك جدّا لئلّا تقطع غير تلك العروق.
When you are finished, instill in the eye the green or red suppository so that its sharpness consumes what remains of the diseased tissue.
If you cannot pick it all up at that time, then dress the eye with something that soothes the eye's pain and leave it for days until its pain subsides and you are safe from the hot swelling.
Then repeat the procedure on it in this same manner until it heals.
This is a picture of the scissors:
The basis of the procedure is that you open the eye with fixed or triangular openers, held by a skilled student, and the head of the patient is in the lap of the student, and another one dries the tears and verifies the gaze in the front of the eye and its back, and you have the choice to start the picking from the top of the eye or from its bottom.
And it's best to dry two hooks on the upper side, one at the end of the corona and the other at its beginning, and hold them between the middle and index fingers.
Then hang hooks from below opposite them. ثم تمسكها بين الخنصر والبنصر
And lift your hand lightly until you see that all the strands have risen.
Cut from the smaller west, if you wish, with scissors, and if you wish, with a fine scalpel.
And insert the probe on a needle and clean all the strands until they rise over the conjunctiva.
And do not cut the dryness, because tears and blood will become difficult (liquify?) for you.
Then cut with scissors what is beyond the corona, from above and from below, so that nothing remains attached except in the cornea.
If you can lift it from the cornea by peeling with the probe, it is better.
Chapter nineteen on returning the feather to the nose.
Doctors call the fistula a fistula.
If you treat it with cautery or with a sharp, burning medication as described previously, and it does not heal, then there is no remedy for it except to incise the swelling when it ripens and extract all the moisture or pus in it until the bone is exposed.
So when the bone is exposed and you see corruption or blackness in it, scrape it with an instrument like this:
And it is called the rough-headed one, made from Indian iron, and its head is round like a button, engraved with the engraving of a file or scalpel, a fine engraving.
You place it on the site of the corruption in the bone, then rotate it between your fingers while clenching your hand slightly until you know that the corruption has been scraped away.
And you do that repeatedly, then you dress the place with drying, astringent medicines.
If the place is sealed and flesh grows in it, and the pus flow stops and it remains for forty days, and it does not regenerate, nor fester, nor does anything happen to it, then know that it has healed, otherwise there is no solution except to return the fistula to the nose opening in this way, which is to expose the bone again with iron or with a sharp medicine. فإذا انكشف العظم فخذ مشعبا على هذه الصورة:
The tip of the instrument should be triangular, and its shaft conical, brought to a point, as you see.
Then place it on the bone itself, and this should be near the suture, and keep your hand a little away from the eye. ثمّ أدر يدك بالمشعب حتّى ينفذ العظم ويحسّ به العليل بأن يجد الريح تخرج منه اذا أمسك يده على أنفه.
Then at this point, treat the area with astringent and drying medications, as I have taught you.
So when the flesh grows and the place hardens, the matter that was flowing outwards will return to the nose, and this will be easier for the patient, God willing.
Chapter Twenty on Pushing Back Protrusions of the Eye
If the eye swells in its entirety, and no damage or impairment occurs in vision, then it is necessary to give the patient a laxative, then bleed him in the cephalic vein.
Then place a cupping glass on the nape of the neck without scarification and perform a gentle suction. ثمّ تضع على العين لطوخا صنع من أقاقيا وصبر ولبان وعنزروت
The method for the compresses is to take many soft rags and fold each rag into four folds, making many of them, then place them one on top of the other to the extent needed by the eye, then tie them firmly with a strong cloth.
And repeat the cupping with suction without scarification.
Then remove the cupping glass and leave the eye bandaged for a day and a night.
If the bandage loosens during that time, then it should be tightened well.
Then remove the bandage after a day and a night as we said.
If you see that the eye has returned to normal, then good, otherwise repeat the poultice, compresses, bandaging, and cupping until it returns to normal.
Chapter twenty-one on cutting the uvea.
If a rupture occurs in the uveal layer, then it swells and protrudes outside the eyelids like a grape, thus disfiguring the person's appearance. وأردت قطعها فالعمل فيها على ما أصف
It is that you insert a needle into the base of the grape-like swelling from bottom to top. ثمّ تدخل إبرة أخرى فيها خيط مثنىّ من ناحية المأق وتنفذها وتدع الإبرة الأولى على حالها
Then you cut the place where the doubled thread is folded and tie some of the swelling around the needle and tighten it well.
Then you remove the needle and place wool moistened with egg white on the eye and leave it until the threads fall off with the swelling.
Then you treat the eye with what strengthens it until the wound heals.
The swelling may also be tightened from all sides with a circle of cloth so that the swelling increases well.
Then it is lanced with a thin scalpel that reaches the depth of the eye, so that the watery fluid flows out and the swelling subsides and withers on the spot.
Then you tighten it until it heals.
Chapter twenty-two on the treatment of leukoderma.
This ailment, which is called 'kamana', is a duration that gathers in the eye, resembling dripping water, but it is not water.
And the way to treat this is that you sit the patient upright on a chair, then you take his head with your hands from both sides and move it until you see the 'duration' move to the bottom of his eye, then it stabilizes and doesn't move, and the light is released, and the patient sees things as he used to see them.
And if it does not descend to the bottom, we know that it is water.
If the descent of the 'duration' is not possible by what we mentioned, then sit the patient between your hands, then take a thin scalpel and make a small incision above the cornea at the junction of the conjunctiva with the cornea in the 'iklil' (limbus) until the substance comes out.  Once it comes out, instill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek and honey have been boiled. Then treat with other treatments until he recovers.
Chapter twenty-three on cupping for the water that descends into the eye.
We have mentioned the types of water in the classification and which one is suitable for the cupping glass, with detailed and explained words, so you take it from there correctly.
Then, you should sit the patient between your hands, squared facing the light near the sun, and tie his healthy eye, tightening it well.
Then you lift his eyelid with your left hand if the eye that has the water is the left eye, or with your right hand if it is the right eye.
Then you place the tip of the cupping glass near the iris, with the thickness of a probe, in the white of the eye itself, from the side of the smaller canthus, then you push the cupping glass with force while rotating it with your hand until it penetrates the white of the eye and you feel with the cupping glass that it has reached something empty.
And it should be that the extent of the cupping glass's going into the depth is equal to the distance that is from the pupil to the end of the blackness, which is the iris of the eye, for you see the copper in the eye of the observer himself, due to the clarity of the cornea.
Then you move the cupping glass upwards to the place where the water is, then you press it downwards repeatedly. If the water descends immediately, then the patient will see whatever his sight opens upon immediately, with the cupping glass in his eye. Then he rests a little. If the water rises, then lower it again without removing the cupping glass.
And when it settles and doesn't rise, remove the cupping glass gently while twisting it with your hand little by little.
Then you dissolve in water a bit of pure Andarani salt and wash the eye with it from the inside, then you place on the outside of the whole eye lint or wool moistened with rose oil and egg white, and you tie the healthy eye with it.
As for us and the people of our time, we put on it ground cumin with egg white.
If the cupping glass does not respond to you for entering the eye due to its hardness, because among people there are those whose eyes are very hard, then you should take the lancet that is called the 'barid,' which is this image:
So you pierce only the conjunctiva itself, and do not go deep in the piercing.
It is only that you tap a fine spot for the lancet, then insert the lancet as we mentioned.
And when your work is complete, prepare for the patient a firm bed in which he sleeps on his back in a dark room, and he refrains from all movements and from coughing, and you make his food what softens his nature, and he does not move his head right or left at all, and the bandage remains as it is until the third day, then you loosen it in that dark room, and test his vision, and show him things, then you return the bandage until the seventh day.
And it is not appropriate that you do that at the time of treatment or after the lancing immediately, but it is appropriate that you avoid that before the water rises quickly with intense looking.
If a hot swelling appears, it is appropriate to unbind the eye before the seventh day and correct that with what calms the swelling, so that when it subsides, then you release his vision and place a veil over his face, training his vision from under it for days while he is in that dark room, then he leaves the room gradually and manages his affairs.
And know that in lancing, the learner cannot do without observation several times, then he proceeds to the work.
And it has reached me from some of the Iraqis that he mentioned that a perforated lancet is made in Iraq that sucks the water with it, and I have not seen anyone in our country do that, nor have I read it in a book of the early books, and it is possible that this is a recent innovation.
And this is a picture of types of lancets for those who are ignorant of them to understand:
It is made specifically of copper. ويكون طرفها بهذه الرقّة بعينها مثلّثة الطرف حادّة،
Chapter twenty-four on the treatment of nasal polyps.
Various excess flesh may grow in the nose, some of which resembles a scorpion with many legs.
And some of it is cancerous flesh, hardened and dark-colored.
And some of it is soft flesh, not dark-colored. So whatever of this flesh is soft, is not malignant or cancerous,
so you should sit the patient before you, facing the sun, and open his nostril, and cast the hook into that flesh, then pull it out, then cut what you reach of it with a fine, sharp scalpel from one side until you know that all the flesh is gone.
If any of it remains that you cannot cut, scrape it with one of the fine instruments gently until nothing of it remains. فإن غلبك الدم او عرض ورم حارّ فقابله بما ينبغى او كان من الأورام الخبيثة فبادر فاكوه حتّى ينقطع الدم وتذهب جميع اللحوم.
Then, after cutting, put vinegar and water or a drink into the nose. فإن انفتح الأنف وسلكت منه الرطوبة الى الحلق فاعلم أنّه قد برئ،
But if the moisture does not flow as it should, know that inside him is growing flesh at the top of the spongy bones that the instrument did not reach by cutting.
At that time, it is necessary to take a somewhat thick linen thread and tie many knots in it, making the distance between each knot the length of a finger or less. ويتحيّل العليل يدسّ طرف الخيط الواحد فى أنفه بمرود او بما أمكنه بعد أن يصنعه مثل الزّر ويجذب ريحه حتّى يصل الى الخيشوم ويخرج على حلقه.
Boys in school often do such a thing, and it is easy for whoever wants to do it.
Then, bring together the two ends of the thread, the one that came out of the mouth and the other that remained in the nose, then use the knots in the thread to saw the flesh, doing so until you know that the flesh has been cut by the knots of the thread.
Then remove the thread and, after wiping the blood, insert a wick into the nose that you have soaked in Egyptian ointment. Do this for three days or more until the ointment consumes all remaining flesh.
Then, lastly, insert a lead tube into the nose for several days until it heals.
If it needs a drying treatment, use that.
And this is a picture of the syringe with which oils and medicines are dripped into the nose:
He places something like a small lamp, open at its reservoir and channel, made of silver or copper.
Similarly, if you wish, you make the tube closed, like a reed, with a flat surface for the perfume oil.
It has a handle at its end, as you see, to hold it when you heat oil in it or what. شئت من العصارات او الأشياء السيّالة،
Chapter twenty-five on warts growing on the tip of the nose.
Often a wart grows on the edge of the nose, it grows and increases with the days until its appearance becomes ugly.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut it off at its first appearance and completely uproot it, then apply to the area either cauterization or a burning medication that acts as cauterization.
If you miss cutting it until it grows, then look: if it is petrified, hard, dark in color, and has little feeling, do not touch it with iron, for it is a cancerous tumor.
And I have often seen those who cut this tumor suffer a great affliction as a result.
If the tumor is soft to the touch, not dark in color, and you see that it is possible to cut it completely, then induce vomiting in the sick person, and cut it without hesitation or delay, and treat the area with something that dries and constricts until it heals.
Chapter twenty-six on suturing the nose, lip, and ear اذاتفرّق اتّصالها عن جرح او نحو ذلك
Know that whenever a separation of connection occurs in one of these cartilages, the treatment rarely succeeds except in some people.
So it is necessary, when something like this happens to someone, to see if the wound is fresh with its blood, to bring the edges of the wound together by stitching, then treat it until it heals.
And if the separation of the connection has separated its lips and each side has become sound, it is necessary to excoriate each side with the thickness of its visible skin until it bleeds, then bring the two lips together by stitching and tighten them, and sprinkle on it ground costus and frankincense, and put over the powder a plaster of date palm ointment or other vulnerary ointments, and leave it tight for two or three days, then loosen it and change the medication, and leave it until the stitches fall out on their own, then treat it with the ointment until it heals.
The method of stitching is to bring together the separation of the connection either with needles as we described in stitching the abdomen, or with thread as I explained to you there.
Chapter twenty-seven on removing the nodules that appear on the lips.
Many people may experience small, hard tumors inside their lips. يشبه بعضها حبّ الكرسنّة وبعضها أصغر وأكبر.
It is necessary to turn the lip outward, make an incision on each nodule, catch it with a hook, and cut it from all sides.
Then, after cutting, pack the area with powdered vitriol until the bleeding stops.
Then, rinse the mouth with vinegar and salt, and treat the areas with astringents until the wounds heal.
Chapter twenty-eight on cutting excess flesh in the gums.
Often, excess flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call epulis (a type of gingival swelling).
It is necessary to hook it with a fishing hook or grasp it with forceps and cut it at its base. وتترك المدّة تسيل او الدم
Then you apply powdered vitriol (hydrated ferrous sulfate) or one of the dried astringent peak substances to the area.
If that flesh returns after the treatment, it often does return. فاقطعه ثانية واكوه فإنّه لا يعود بعد الكىّ
Chapter twenty-nine on filing the teeth with iron.
Rough, ugly scales may gather on the surfaces of the teeth, inside and out, and between the gums. وقد تسودّ وتصفرّ وتخضرّ حتّى يصل من ذلك فساد الى اللثة وتقبح الأسنان لذلك.
So, you should sit the patient between your hands with his head in your lap and scrape the molar and the tooth in which the scales and the thing resembling sand have appeared to you until nothing of it remains. وكذلك تفعل بالسواد والخضرة والصفرة وغير ذلك حتّى تنقى.
If what is in it is gone from the first scraping, then fine, otherwise you repeat the scraping on it another day, and a second, and a third, until you reach the goal in what you want.
And know that the molar needs scrapers of various forms and many shapes according to what is prepared for your work because the scraper with which the molar is scraped from the inside is different from the scraper with which it is scraped from the outside. والذى يجرد به بين الأضراس على صورة أخرى.
And these are several forms of scrapers that you should have, all prepared.
Chapter Thirty on the Extraction of Teeth
It is appropriate to treat the tooth for its pain with every possible remedy and to be hesitant about extracting it, for there is no replacement for it if it is extracted, because it is a noble substance, even if there is no alternative but to extract it.
So it is appropriate, if the ailing person is determined to extract it, that you ascertain and verify that the aching tooth is indeed the one, for often the pain deceives the ailing person, and he thinks that it is in the healthy tooth, so he extracts it, and then the pain does not go away until the diseased tooth is extracted.
We have seen this from the actions of cuppers repeatedly.
So if you are certain about the aching tooth itself, then it is appropriate to incise around the tooth with a lancet that has some strength, until you loosen the gum from every side, then move it with your fingers or with the gentle forceps first, little by little, until you loosen it, then at that point secure it firmly with the large forceps while the ailing person's head is between your knees, firmly held so he doesn't move, then pull the tooth straight so you don't break it.
If it does not come out, then take one of those instruments and insert it under it from every direction gently, and keep moving it as you did before.
And if the tooth is perforated or corroded, it is appropriate to fill that hole with a piece of cloth and plug it well with the tip of a thin file so that it does not shatter when you pull on it with the forceps, and it is appropriate to be thorough in incising around the gum from every side carefully, and be careful with your effort so you don’t break it, and some of it remains, causing the ailing person a calamity greater than his first pain.
And beware of doing what the ignorant cuppers do in their haste and rushing into extracting it without using what we described, for they often inflict great calamities upon people, the least of which is that the tooth breaks and all or some of its roots remain. أن يقلع ببعض عظام الفكّ كما شاهدناه مرارا،
Then after extracting it, he should rinse his mouth with wine or with vinegar and salt.
If bleeding occurs from the area, and this often happens, then crush some vitriol and pack the area with it, or otherwise cauterize it if the vitriol does not benefit you.
The shape of the gentle forceps with which you move the tooth first should be long-tipped, short-handled, and thick so that they do not bend when you grip the tooth with them.
And this is the shape of the large forceps:
It should be, as you see, thick in the handles so that when gripped it does not give way or bend, and short in the extremities.
And let it be made of Indian iron or of well-wrought, polished steel at the extremities. وفى طرفها أضراس يدخل بعضها فى بعض فتقبض قبضا محكما وثيقا
And the extremities may be made in the form of a file, and it will also be strong in gripping.
Chapter thirty-one on the extraction of the roots of the molars and the removal of the jaw bones.
The broken one, if upon extraction of the tooth a root remains that has broken, فينبغى أن تضع على الموضع قطنة بالسمن يوما او يومين حتّى يسترخى الموضع
It will have been made like a file from the inside or like a rasp.
If it does not respond to you to come out with these hooks, فينبغى أن تحفر على الأصل
Short at the end, slightly thick, and it should not be watered/polished, lest it break.
If the bone comes out with that, otherwise resort to these other instruments, whose image this is.
The first is triangular at the end, with some thickness in it.
Another nice triangular image/diagram:
And with other instruments and irons that were mentioned previously in the filing of molars
And we may also use this instrument that resembles a large fishhook, which this is its image
Triangular, the curved end having some slight thickness so that it does not break, and it should be unpolished.
And know that the instruments for molars are numerous, and likewise the other instruments are almost innumerable, and the experienced and skilled craftsman may invent instruments for himself according to what the work and the diseases themselves guide him to, because among diseases there are some for which the ancients did not mention instruments due to the difference in their types.
So if a bone of the jaw or one of the bones of the mouth is broken or decayed, then probe it in its place with what is suitable for it from one of these instruments and hooks that were mentioned for extracting roots, and we use a forceps, this is its form:
It should have some slight thickness to hold the bone in place so it doesn't slip until the bone comes out.
And we treat the area with the appropriate medicines for that.
If the bone has some slight putrefaction, then scrape it from its putrefaction and blackness until it is clean, then treat it until it heals.
Chapter thirty-two on the spreading of molars that grow on top of others.
If the molars grow in a way other than their natural course, they make the face ugly.
And especially if this happens in women and slaves, then you should look, and if the molar has grown behind another molar and it is not possible to spread it or file it, then extract it.
And if it is attached to another molar, then cut it with this instrument which is pictured here:
And it resembles a small beak. ولتكن من حديد هندىّ حادّة الطرف جدّا
And your cutting of it should be over many days, due to the hardness of the tooth. ولئلّا تزعزع غيرها من الأضراس
then file it with a file of Indian steel which has this form:
It should all be from India, and its point should be very finely engraved, like the file with which needles are made.
File the tooth with it little by little over many days, gently, so that you do not shake the tooth and it falls out. ثمّ تملّسه آخرا وتجرده ببعض المجارد
And if a tooth has been broken and it bothers the tongue when speaking, then it should also be filed until the roughness of the break disappears, and it becomes even and smooth, and does not harm the tongue, nor does it spoil speech.
Chapter thirty-three on joining loose molars with silver threads or with gold threads.
If the front molars become loose and move due to a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot bite on anything edible lest they fall out, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, but the treatment has not been successful
then the trick is to tie them with a gold or silver thread, and gold is better because silver tarnishes and decays after a few days, while gold remains in its state forever and is not affected by that.
The thread should be medium in thinness and thickness, as much as can fit between the molars.
And the method of tying is that you take the thread and insert its bend between the two healthy molars, then weave with the ends of the thread between the loose molars, whether one or more, until you reach the healthy molar on the other side, then you return the weaving to the side you started from.
And tighten your hand gently and wisely so that it does not move at all, and your tightening of the thread should be at the roots of the molars so that it does not escape.
Then cut the ends of the excess thread with scissors, gather them, twist them with the husk, and hide them between the healthy molar and the loose molar so that they do not hurt the tongue. ثمّ تترك هكذا مشدودة ما بقيت
If it becomes loose or breaks, tighten it with another thread, and they will enjoy it like this for the rest of their life.
This is a picture of the molars and the method of tying in two healthy molars and two loose molars, as you see.
And one or two teeth may return after falling out, to their places, and become fixed, as we have described, and remain.
And only a skilled and delicate craftsman does that.
And he may carve bone from the bones of cattle, and make from it the shape of a tooth and place it in the location from which the tooth has gone, and fasten it as we have said, and it remains and benefits from that.
The thirty-fourth chapter on cutting the ligament that appears under the tongue and prevents speech.
This frenulum that appears under the tongue may be either natural, with which a person is born, or accidental, from a wound that has healed.
The procedure for it is to open the patient's mouth with his head in your lap and lift his tongue, then cut that frenulum transversely until the tongue is released from its restriction.
If there is some hardness and knotting in it, and that is from the healing of a wound, then insert a hook into it and incise it transversely until the frenulum is severed and the knot is loosened.
Beware that the incision is not deep in the flesh, lest you cut an artery there and cause bleeding.
Then he should rinse his mouth after the cutting with rose water or with vinegar and cold water.
Then place a wick of linen under the tongue, which the patient holds every night so that it does not reattach.
If bleeding occurs, put powdered vitriol on the area. فإن غلبك الدم فاكو الموضع بمكواة عدسيّة تصلح لذلك ثمّ عالجه بسائر العلاج حتّى يبرأ
Chapter thirty-five on the extraction of the frog generated under the tongue.
A swelling may occur under the tongue, resembling a small frog, which prevents the tongue from its natural function. وربّما عظم حتّى يملأ الفم،
and the treatment for it is to open the patient's mouth facing the sun and examine the swelling. If you see it dark in color or black and hard, and the patient feels no sensation in it, do not touch it, for it is cancer.
But if it is tending towards white and has moisture in it, insert a hook into it and incise it with a fine scalpel and free it from every side, فإن غلبك الدم فى حين عملك فضع عليه زاجا مسحوقا حتّى ينقطع الدم ثمّ عد الى عملك حتّى تخرجه بكماله
Then have him rinse his mouth with vinegar and salt, then treat him with all the other appropriate remedies until he recovers.
Chapter thirty-six on the treatment of swelling of the tonsils and what grows in the throat from other swellings.
Swellings resembling those that appear externally, called tonsils, may occur inside the throat.
If you treat them with what I mentioned in the chapter and they do not heal, then observe: if the swelling is hard, livid in color, and has little sensation, do not touch it with an instrument.
And if it is red in color and its base is thick, do not touch it with an instrument either, for fear of bleeding. بل اتركه حتّى ينضج فإمّا أن تبطّه وإمّا أن يتفجّر من ذاته.
And if it is white in color, round, and its base is thin, this is the one that should be cut.
And the procedure for it is that you look before the operation, if its hot swelling has subsided completely or decreased somewhat, then you should sit the patient beside the sun with his head in your lap, and open his mouth, and take an assistant to stand in front of you to press his tongue down with an instrument like this image:
It is made of silver or copper, and it is thin like a knife.
So when you press the tongue with it, and the swelling becomes clear to you, and your sight falls upon it
then take a hook and insert it into the tonsil and pull it outwards as much as possible without pulling any of the membranes with it.
Then you cut it with an instrument of this form: تشبه المقصّ الا أنّ طرفيها منعطفان
It is made from Indian iron or Damascene steel.
If this instrument is not available وإلّا فاقطعها بمبضع
So after you cut one tonsil, you cut the other one in the same way,
Then after the cutting, the patient gargles with cold water or vinegar and water,
If bleeding occurs, gargle with water in which pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves or similar astringents have been boiled until the bleeding stops ثمّ تعالجه حتّى يبرأ،
And other tumors may grow in the throat besides the tonsils, and you cut them in the same way as I mentioned in cutting the tonsils.
I treated a woman with a tumor that had grown inside her throat, tending towards numbness, with little sensation, which almost blocked the throat وكانت المرأة تتنفّس عن مجرى ضيّق
and the woman was breathing through a narrow passage وكان قد منعها الأكل وشرب الماء
and two branches had risen from the tumor until they came out of her nostrils
so I hurried and inserted a hook into one of them ثمّ جذبته فانجذب منه قطعة صالحة
then I cut it where I reached it from the nostril
then I did the same with what protruded from the other nostril
then I opened her mouth and pressed down her tongue ثمّ أغرزت الصنّارة فى نفس الورم
so we continued to cut from that tumor repeatedly for a long time
and the tumor would replace what was cut حتّى طال بى وبها ذلك
So I devised a plan and cauterized the tumor inside the throat from above فتوقّف عن الزيادة
then I traveled away from the area and I did not know what God did with her after me.
Chapter thirty-seven on the excision of the uvula tumor which is called grape.
If a catarrh descends to the uvula and swells and is white and oblong, then it is called 'amood'.
And if it is thick at the bottom and round, then it is called 'inabah'.
If it is treated with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment is not effective, and you see that the hot swelling has subsided and it is thin, then it should be cut.
And what is of it gathered and round and does not have length and is bloody or the color of pus or black or has no sensation, then it should be avoided cutting it, for there is danger in it for the patient.
Then it is necessary, if you see it in the manner that I mentioned of its whiteness and length, that you seat the patient by the sun and compress his tongue with the instrument which was previously described. ثمّ تغرز الصنّارة فى العنبة وتجذبها الى أسفل وتقطعها بأحد الآلتين اللتين ذكرتهما فى قطع اللوزتين
And it is necessary that you do not cut from it except that which exceeds the natural order without addition, because if you cut more from it you will harm the voice and speech.
Then after the cutting, use what we described in cutting the tonsils and treat it until it heals.
If the patient is afraid of its cutting, then it is necessary that you use a trick in cauterizing it without fear or caution.
And the way of cauterizing it is only with the strong medicine, which is that you place the head of the patient in your lap, then you compress his tongue with the instrument that we mentioned. ثمّ تأخذ من الماء الحادّ الذى ذكرت فى باب الكىّ وتعجن به جيرا غير مطفأ وتجعله لا ثخينا ولا رقيقا وتملأ منه تقعير هذه الآلة وهذه صورتها:
Its end, in which you place the medication, has a concavity like the concavity of a cautery spoon.
And you place the instrument with the medication on the uvula itself, with the patient lying on his side so that the saliva flows from his mouth from inside his throat, lest anything descend from it into his throat and harm him.
Then you hold the medication with your hand and you squeeze it on the uvula for about half an hour until you see that it has blackened and the sting of the medication has subsided.
And if you wish, you can take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a cautery iron, and soak the cotton in the medication, and insert the cautery iron with the cotton in a tube from above until the cotton adheres to the uvula; you do this repeatedly until you achieve what you want from cauterizing the uvula, then you leave it, for it will wither and fall off after three or four days.
If you need to reapply the medication, you reapply it.
And after the cauterization, you wipe around the uvula with cotton soaked in ghee and dry the medication around it with it.
Then he gargles with cold water and is treated externally with poultices and internally with gargles until he recovers.
So, this type of treatment is safer than excision and further from fear.
And the uvula can also be treated with something gentler than cauterization and excision: it is treated with fumigation in this manner. يؤخذ فوذنج وزوفا وصعتر وسذاب وشيح وبابونج وقيصوم ونحوها من الحشائش فتجمعها كلّها او بعضها فى قدر وتغمر فى الخلّ وتغلى والقدر مطيّنة بطين الحكمة وتكون فى وسط الغطاء ثقبة تركّب عليها الآلة المجوّفة على هذه الصفة تصنع من فضّة او نحاس:
And you insert the end that contains the pomegranate into the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the uvula through the tube until the uvula is well fumigated.
Then you repeat it several times until it withers.
And beware of doing this treatment at the first appearance of the swelling, because it often increases the swelling. وإنّما ينبغى أن تفعل ذلك عند انحطاط ورمها الحارّ
If this instrument is not available to you, then take a reed and attach an eggshell to its end so that the patient's mouth does not burn, because the eggshell prevents the heat of the vapor from burning the mouth.
And this is among the best treatments, along with its safety.
Chapter thirty-eight on the removal of thorns and what gets stuck in the throat other than that.
Often a bone, a fishbone, or something else gets stuck in the throat.
It is necessary to remove from it what is visible to the eye after pressing the tongue with the instrument in the sunlight so that what is in the throat becomes clear to you.
And what is not visible to you and is hidden in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit before his food is digested in his stomach. فربّما خرج الشىء الناشب بالقئ
Or the patient swallows a piece of turnip or the root of lettuce. او يتبلّع لقمة من خبز يابس
Do this several times. فكثيرا ما تلصق الشوكة او العظم فيها وتخرج
If it does not come out with what we have mentioned, then use a lead instrument in this manner:
It should be slightly thicker than the sound, and at its end there is a curve that the patient inserts gently into his throat, while raising his head upwards. ويتحفّظ من مسّ حنجرته لئلّا يحدث به سعال.
And he pushes the bone or thorn with it, or the physician inserts it with his hand, and the patient's insertion of it is better because of his knowledge of the location of the embedded thing. ويدفع الى أسفل او يجذب يده بالآلة الى فوق كلّ ذلك على قدر ما يتهيّأ له حتّى يخرج،
Chapter thirty-nine on removing the leech stuck in the throat
If you treat the leech with what we mentioned in the division of treatment with medicines and it does not succeed, then look at that time in the throat of the sick person in the sun after you press his tongue with the instrument that was described to you, and if your sight falls on the leech, pull it with a small hook or with a smooth, tight piece of date fiber.
If you are not able to do it with it, then take a hollow tube and insert it into the throat of the sick person near the leech, then insert into the inside of the tube a piece of iron heated by fire; you do this several times and the sick person abstains from water for his entire day, then he takes a bowl filled with cold water and opens his mouth in it and gargles with it and does not swallow a drop of it and moves the water from time to time with his hand, for the leech will fall on the spot when it senses the water.
If it does not come out with what we described, then fumigate the throat with urine and with asafoetida with the instrument that was described in the fumigation of the uvula, you do that several times, for it will fall.
And the way to work in fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are embers heated by fire, and the pot is covered with a lid in the middle of which is a hole, and you install in that hole the end of the instrument, then you throw in the incense, and the sick person puts his mouth at the end of the tube and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out until he knows that the smoke has reached his throat, for the leech will fall on the spot.
If it does not fall, then the fumigation is repeated several times and the sick person endures thirst and eats salty things and garlic and does not drink water, so it must come out with this procedure.
And this is a picture of an instrument with which you pull the leech from the throat if the sight falls on it, and it resembles hooks, as you see, except that it has this curvature that enters the throat, and its two ends resemble the mouth of a bird, in it is the roughness of a file; if it bites on something, it does not leave it.
And another instrument with which the tongue is depressed, and it is a wide ring of iron, as much as the mouth can accommodate above the tongue, enters the mouth standing on its side, so the mouth remains open without the patient's will. ولا يستطيع أن يقلعها البتّة حتّى تنحيها:
(Description of the instrument with which the mouth is opened according to this exact measurement)
The fortieth chapter: in it is made of the discussion about lancing tumors and incising them.
Tumors are of many various types, as will be mentioned one by one in this book, and they differ in their lancing and incising in two aspects: one is the type of tumor itself and the humors it contains.
The second aspect is the location in the body where they occur, because a tumor occurring in the head is different from a tumor occurring in the anus, and a tumor occurring in a fleshy area is different from a tumor occurring in a joint, each one having its own treatment rule.
Some tumors should not be lanced until the pus in them has matured and is complete, and some should be lanced while they are fresh and have not fully matured, such as tumors that are close to the joints, because if a tumor occurs near a joint and its condition prolongs until what is around it putrefies, it may damage the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing chronicity of that limb, or the tumor may be near a major organ, so if you delay its lancing until it matures, you will harm that major organ, or it may be near the anus, so you lance it fresh.
It is necessary to lance the fresh, not fully matured tumor that is near the anus so that the depth does not putrefy and penetrate into the anus, becoming a fistula and becoming incurable.
You should know the time to lance tumors that have fully matured, which is when the pain of the tumor subsides, the fever disappears, the redness and throbbing decrease, the head of the tumor softens, and other signs.
The lancing should be performed at the lowest point of the tumor if possible, so that it is easier for the fluid to flow downwards, or at the thinnest and most protruding point of the tumor.
The lancing should be lengthwise along the body if the tumors are in areas such as the hands and feet, muscles, tendons, nerves, arteries, and in general in all flat areas without bending.
As for those that bend, the lancing should be done according to that area. If the tumor is in fleshy areas, it is best to leave it until it is fully matured, as we have said, because if you lance it before that, the flow of pus from it will be prolonged and it will be very harmful and dirty, and perhaps its edges and depth will harden.
Some tumors may be lanced across the body when necessary or according to the needs of the limb.
You should use a single lancing for small tumors and a wide lancing or multiple incisions for large tumors, according to the size of the tumor.
Some tumors may require the skin to be scraped and cut if it has become like a rag and is dead, such as what occurs in many boils and abscesses.
Some are incised with a three-cornered incision, some are cut in the shape of a myrtle leaf, like inguinal tumors, and some use a circular or crescent-shaped incision, and so on.
Those that do not have a head, such as smooth, flat tumors, should only be lanced simply.
If the tumor is large and has accumulated a lot of fluid and you lance it, you should not rush to remove all the pus at that time, but rather remove some of it, then bandage the tumor until the next day, then remove some more pus, doing this gradually until you remove all of it, especially if the patient is weak, a pregnant woman, a small child, or an elderly person, because the vital spirit often dissolves with the sudden removal of pus, so the patient may die without you realizing it, so be very careful about this.
After lancing these tumors, you should wipe the wound and examine it. If the wound of the tumor is small or the incision is single and simple, use linen or worn cotton thread. If the tumor is large and the incisions are numerous, you should insert a wick into each incision until they reach each other.
If some of the skin of the tumor has been cut or scraped, you should fill it with worn cotton or linen lint without moisture and bandage it until the third day, then remove it and treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If bleeding occurs during your work, use cold water and vinegar after soaking a linen cloth in them and applying it to the bleeding area several times.
If the bleeding continues, you should use the management, treatment, and peaks that we have described in many places in this book and in the division.
If you are in the winter season and the location of the tumor is rich in nerves, you should moisten the pads with hot wine and oil and place them on the area.
If you are in the summer and the areas are fleshy, you should apply pads soaked in cold water and oil or cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said, then you should untie the tumor, wipe it, and use similar treatment until it heals.
This is what you need to know about the treatment of tumors in general. As for the detailed method, I have mentioned each tumor and how to treat it, categorized and summarized.
Chapter forty-one on incising the tumors that occur on the scalp.
Small tumors appear on the scalp. وهى من أنواع السلع تحويها صفاقات هى لها ظروف كأنّها حوصلة الدجاجة.
And its types are many, some of them are fatty. ومنها ما تحوى رطوبة تشبه الحمأة.
And there is no danger in incising them and extracting their contents, unless an artery obstructs you when you incise it.
The procedure for incising it is to first probe it with the instrument whose image comes after this, which is called al-Midass (the probe), so that you know what it contains.
So if what it contains is moisture, incise it lengthwise with a simple incision in this manner:
And begin the incision from line B to line C. فإذا تفرّغت الرطوبة فاسلخ الكيس الذى كان يحوى تلك الرطوبة واقطعه جميعه ولا تترك منه شيئا البتّة فكثيرا ما يعود اذا بقى منه شىء
Then dip cotton in the Egyptian ointment if it is available, and if not, in salt water, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day, as it will consume what remains of the sac.
Then repeat the application of the cotton with the Egyptian ointment a second and third time, if needed, until you are certain that nothing of the sac remains.
Then treat the wound with ointments until it heals.
And if the swelling contains a fatty mass, incise it in this manner. شقّا مصلّبا والق الصنانير فى شفتى الجرح واسلخه من كلّ جهة.
If an artery obstructs you, do what I described to you later, and do the same for the swelling if it is hardened from the incision, and the treatment is the same as I mentioned.
The incision on the hardened swelling is easier because it has little blood and moisture, and some of these swellings that are in the head in some people may have no moisture at all, and that is because I incised a swelling in the head of an old woman, and I found the swelling like a hard, rough, white stone, I could not break it, and if someone threw it, it would injure him.
And what was of the other swellings occurring in the head other than this, such as the swellings that appear in the heads of children and at the bases of the ears, incise them all with a simple incision and make its bottom from its lower part to facilitate the flow of the material to the bottom, then treat it with what is appropriate for it of treatment.
The forty-second chapter on the incision on the scrofulas that appear in the neck.
These tumors frequently occur in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groins, and they may occur throughout the body.
Those that occur in the neck can be single or multiple. ويتولّد بعضها من بعض.
And the types of these scrofulous tumors are many: some are hardened, some contain fluids, and some are malignant and do not respond to treatment.
So, if I find one of them that feels good to the touch, and its appearance is close to the color of the skin, and it moves in every direction, and it is not attached to a nerve of the neck, nor to a vein, nor to an artery, and it is not deep, then it should be incised with a simple incision from top to bottom of the growth in this manner, from line C to line B.
And skin it from every side, and stretch the lips of the skin with a hook or with two hooks, or with many hooks, if you need that, as we said regarding head tumors, and extract it little by little, and be careful not to cut a vein or a nerve.
And let the scalpel not be very sharp, lest your hand cuts more, or the patient moves, so you cut what you don't need to cut.
If you cut a vein or an artery and it hinders you from working, then put in the wound crushed vitriol or some of the powders that stop the blood, and tighten the wound and leave it until the intensity of the tumor subsides, the wound relaxes and starts to suppurate, then the blood will stop then, so return to your work until you are finished.
Then search with your index finger, if other small tumors remained, then cut them and clean them.
If there is a large vein at the base of the tumor, then it is appropriate not to cut that tumor from its base, but it is appropriate to tie it with a doubled tight thread and leave it until it falls by itself without harm, then fill the wound with worn cotton having dipped it in the Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
And if you cut the whole tumor, then it is appropriate to bring together the lips of the wound and sew it immediately after you know that no excess remains at all, but if you see that some excess remains due to the size of the tumor, then you should aim to cut it to its origin and base, and use stitching and what we mentioned.
And for tumors that contain fluids, poultice them with a simple poultice where their ripeness appears to you, and make the poultice from the lower part, as we said, then after the poultice, use the wick with the Egyptian ointment and the like to eat away what remains of the corruption, until you see the wound has become clean, then treat it with ointments that promote flesh growth until it heals.
Chapter forty-three, on incising the larynx due to a swelling occurring inside the throat.
The ancients mentioned this incision in the larynx, but I have not seen anyone in our country perform it, and this is the order of their words.
As for those with angina, they should avoid incising the larynx, as they will not benefit from it because all the vessels and the lungs are diseased.
But for those who have a hot swelling in the mouth, throat, or tonsils, if there is no ailment in the trachea, it is necessary to use the incision of the larynx to escape the damage that results from choking.
So, if we want to do that, we should incise the larynx below three or four rings of the trachea, a small horizontal incision between two rings, as much as the incision is in the membrane, not in the cartilage, and this place is suitable for the incision because it is devoid of flesh and blood vessels are far from it.
If the practitioner is cowardly, he should stretch the skin of the throat with a hook, then incise the skin until, when he reaches the trachea, he avoids the blood vessels if he sees any of them, then he incises the membrane that we described.
The incision of the trachea is indicated by the phlegm that comes out of it with what is pierced and by the interruption of the voice, and you leave the wound open for a while, so when the time in which choking is feared is over, the lips of the skin wound are brought together and stitched alone without the cartilage, then the medicines that grow flesh are used until it heals.
The author of this book said, "The explanation of all these words that we have narrated is only if they see that the patient's throat has been blocked by one of these swellings that they mentioned, and the patient is near death, and his breathing is about to stop, they go to incise the larynx so that the patient can breathe a little through the wound site and be saved from death.
And they were only ordered to leave the wound open until the course of the illness is over, and its course is three days or so, so then they were ordered to suture the wound and treat it until it heals.
And what I witnessed myself is that a servant took a knife and put it to her throat and cut some of the trachea with it, so I was called to treat her, and I found her gurgling like a slaughtered animal, so I uncovered the wound and found the blood that came out of the wound was little, so I knew that she had not cut a vein or a jugular vein, and the air was coming out of the wound, so I proceeded and stitched the wound and treated it until it healed.
And nothing happened to the servant except hoarseness in the voice, nothing more, and she returned after a few days to her best condition, so from this we say that there is no danger in incising the larynx.
The forty-fourth chapter on incising the swelling that appears on the larynx from the outside. ويسمّى فيلة الحلقوم
This swelling, which is called "fīlat al-ḥalqūm" ("elephant of the larynx"), is a large swelling, the color of the flesh. وهو فى النساء كثير.
It is of two types: either it is natural or it is accidental.
As for the natural, there is no remedy for it.
And as for the accidental, it is of two kinds: one resembles lipoma-like goods, and the other kind resembles the swelling that results from a thickening of the artery, and there is danger in incising it, so it is not appropriate to apply iron to it at all, except what is small of it. إن سبرتها وفتشّتها بالمدّس فألفيتها تشبه السلعة الشحميّة ولم تكن متعلّقة بشىء من العروق فشقّها كما تشقّ على السلع وتخرجها بما يحويها من الكيس إن كانت فى كيس وإلّا فاستقص جميعها.
Chapter forty-five, on fissuring in different kinds of goods/commodities.
Merchandise has many types, and I have mentioned all of its types in the classification.
And it is necessary that we explain here the difference between merchandise and abscess, as it is problematic.
So I say that with an abscess there is heat, fever, and frightening pains until the boiling of the excess subsides and the putrefaction is complete, at which point the fever and the acuteness subside.
With merchandise, there is neither heat, nor fever, nor pain, and it is contained in a peritoneal sac that is its special container, and it is the color of the body, and its beginning is like a chickpea, and it becomes like a duck, and bigger and smaller, and it is of two types, either fatty or it contains moisture, and the colors of the moisture are many, as I mentioned in the classification.
So, when you come to treat merchandise, it is appropriate to probe and examine it first with the instrument called the probe, as its image comes in the chapter after this.
The method for examining all tumors and merchandise is that you take this instrument and insert it in the softest place you find in the tumor while you rotate your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has penetrated the skin, then press your hand according to the size of the tumor.
Then take out the probe and look at what comes out after it. If flowing moisture comes out, whatever color it may be, then incise it with a simple incision as I mentioned in other tumors. And if no moisture comes out after the probe, know that it is fatty, so incise it with a hardened incision in this way, as I have taught you.
And hang it with hooks, and skin the skin from each side gently, and preserve the sac if you are able to remove it intact with the merchandise.
If the sac ruptures during the procedure and you are unable to remove it intact, this happens often, so remove it piece by piece until nothing remains of it, because if something remains of it, little or much, the merchandise will mostly return.
If it overcomes you and a little of it remains, cauterize the wound when you are finished with some sharp, corrosive peaks, and tighten the wound and place over it something that soothes the hot tumor, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
If the merchandise is large, then stitch its lips and treat it with what heals.
If you encounter a pulsating or non-pulsating vein and bleeding occurs, immediately cauterize the area with powdered vitriol and leave it tight for two or three days until the wound putrefies and the boiling of the blood subsides, then return to cutting what remains of the merchandise.
