If you prefer, you can apply a small straight splint to stabilize the fracture and prevent movement. If the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the middle, index, little, or ring finger, align it and tie it with the adjacent healthy finger, or tie them all together in sequence, which is better, or apply a small straight splint as we mentioned for the thumb. Check during your treatment and after it for hot swelling and treat it accordingly whenever anything of this happens, as described repeatedly.
Chapter Fourteen on the Reduction of a Femur Fracture
The femur bone often breaks and is perceptible to the senses because it turns forward and backward.
Its mending is done by tightening a bandage above the fracture and another bandage below the fracture, while the patient is lying on his face.
Then an assistant stretches each bandage to its side moderately, if the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
But if it is close to the origin of the femur, it is necessary to tighten a soft bandage, either from wool or similar, at the origin of the femur towards the pubis, so that the stretching is upwards, and the other bandage below the fracture.
Similarly, if the fracture is near the knee, let the bandage be near the knee so that the stretching is downwards.
Then the physician straightens the bone with both hands until he restores it to its natural form, and the bone unites well.
Then it is necessary to apply the bandage and tightening if no hot swelling occurs to the limb. فإن حدث فيه الورم فاتركه أيّاما حتّى يسكن الورم الحارّ ثمّ ارجع الى علاجه
As for its tightening, it is necessary to twist a solid, wide turban over the fracture two or three times, and whatever is left over remains.
Then twist the leg until the heel is at the origin of the buttock, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg near the knee from below, and the ends of the thread become from above on both sides. ثمّ تدير على الساق والفخذ ما فضل من العمامة
Then place the splints on the thigh at the fracture site itself, and place one of them on the leg bone.
Then fill the gap between the thigh and the leg with soft cloths to level the tightening.
Then start with strong tightening from the middle over the fracture site, three or four turns, and the further you move the bandage from the fracture site, let your tightening be less, softer, and looser.
Then go to the ends of the thread that you had inserted between the thigh and the leg, and tie with it the adjacent splints from above, then pass the ends of the thread down until you reach the man's ankle, and tighten with them also the ends of the splints from the other side so that the bandage does not move from its place.
Then leave the tightening on it as long as no erosion, swelling, inflammation, or the like occurs to the limb. فإن حدث شىء من ذلك فبادر بحلّه وأصلح ما حدث من ذلك كلّه على ما ذكرنا مرارا
If there is a splinter in the bone that pricks, it is necessary to straighten it if you can, otherwise cut on it and remove it, and treat the wound as mentioned earlier until it heals.
This fracture of the femur may be tightened without adding the leg to the splints, as we mentioned in the humerus and forearm.
Except that its mending in this way does not cause lameness to the patient, and if it is mended alone without adding the leg to it, its owner will inevitably limp forever.
And know that the femur heals in fifty days, or a little more or a little less, all according to the difference in temperaments and other conditions.
Chapter Fifteen: On the Fracture of the Patella
The patella rarely fractures, but it is often subject to bruising.
If it does fracture, it will either be a fissure or a comminuted fracture into pieces. ويكون ذلك مع جرح وغير جرح
Its treatment is to align the separated parts with your fingers until they are joined and fitted together, to the best of your ability, gently and skillfully.
Then apply a bandage, and over it a rounded splint, if needed, and tie it firmly as appropriate.
Then treat all the conditions we have described for other fractures, such as hot swelling and the like, by addressing each symptom with what is appropriate for it until it heals.
Chapter Sixteen on the Reduction of a Fracture of the Leg
The leg has two bones, one thick, called the tibia, and the other thin, called the fibula. They are subject to the same types of fractures as the bones of the arm, and therefore their treatment is the same as the treatment of the arm, and the procedure is one.
If both bones are broken, the leg will turn in all directions.
If the thinner bone is broken, the leg will turn forward.
And if the thicker bone is broken and it happens from below, it is something that is not hidden from you. فاستعمل المدّ والتسوية وربط الجبائر على حسب ذلك سواء إلّا أنّه ينبغى إن كان كسر الساق كسرا فاحشا ذا شظايا كثيرة أن يكون المدّ أقلّ وأخفّ وترفق جهدك بجبره،
In the leg, there is something extra in the procedure compared to the arm, which is that when you have aligned the splints and finished all your work, take two thin strips of pine wood, which are used in leveling rooms, that are placed between the cracks of the planks, or they can be from palm leaf ribs, or similar, and choose from them those that have a little thickness and are not thin, and let their length be the length of the leg from the knee to the bottom.
Then wrap a cloth around each one twice along its length, and place one on the leg and the other on the other side, and let them be from the knee to the bottom of the foot.
Then tie the two thin strips in three places, at the ends and the middle, for by this restraint the leg is prevented from tilting right and left and is well stabilized.
A wooden gutter may be used along the length of the leg and placed in it to protect it from movement, and it is most important to do this in a fracture, especially if it is accompanied by a wound.
Then check the leg every day and take great care of it for swelling or inflation or any of that, so whenever anything of that happens, treat it with what is necessary until it heals.
And the leg bone heals in thirty days or so.
Chapter seventeen on the fracture of the bones of the leg and fingers.
As for the heel, it does not suffer a fracture at all.
As for the bones of the leg, they may suffer a fracture, and the toes also rarely suffer a fracture, but rather they suffer a bruise in most cases.
If the bones of the leg suffer a fracture and you see that those bones have overlapped, let the patient place his foot on the ground upright like a walker, then you stand and place your foot on the raised part of those bones, then step on it and straighten it until it returns to its place.
Then carry the bandage and the splint from above and place under the sole of the foot a small board that has two flat ends.
Then tighten the foot tightly after wrapping it with rags and all that you need.
When three or four days have passed for him, release the bandage, for you will find the bones straightened, whether they were broken or dislocated, so the procedure is as you see.
But if some of the toes are broken, set them and straighten them according to what I described to you in setting the fingers of the hand. ثمّ اجعل للأصبع المكسورة جبيرة على طول الأصبع ولتكن أعرض منها قليلا
Then place under the foot this board that I described to you and tighten it tightly.
If the broken bones are two or three or more, then put on each toe a splint of its size inserted in a soft cloth and tighten the board at the bottom of the foot, and let each end of the board rest outside the sole of the foot to secure it well.
And you should not forget to observe all that we have mentioned to you in the rest of the fracture, of the symptoms that we have mentioned, and treat each symptom with what is appropriate.
Chapter Eighteen on the fracture of the woman's clitoris and the pubic bone and the man's penis.
When a woman's vulva is fractured, sit her cross-legged, then bend her slightly towards her back, and let someone hold her from behind. Then the midwife should pack her vulva with cotton until it is full and becomes like a ball in her vulva. Then shake the woman and lift her back slightly, so that the cotton comes out until it is at the entrance of the vulva like a ball and the bone fracture returns to place.
Then place a support on her back, and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton gently until she urinates and return it in the same way you inserted it first. Then she returns to her initial support.
Do this for seven days or so, and it will heal.
If you wish, take a sheep's bladder and tie a reed tube to its opening, and insert the whole bladder into her vulva, then blow strongly into the tube until the bladder inflates inside the vulva, and the fracture will return to place.
Then pack it with cotton and stay for days as we described until it heals.
As for when the pubic bone of a man or woman is fractured, use what we described for the hip bone to repair and straighten it.
The correct approach in these strange fractures, which rarely occur, especially for someone with some experience who understands this book of mine well, should not be hidden from you, because the fracture itself in most cases guides you to the correct way to repair and tighten it, so understand.
As for a man's penis, if it is fractured, take the gullet of a goose and insert the penis into it, then place a bandage of cloth on it and bind it and leave it for three days or so until it heals.
Chapter nineteen on the reduction of bone fractures if they are with a wound.
It is advisable for one who has experienced a fracture with a wound, especially if the bone is large, such as the femur or humerus or similar, to immediately phlebotomize him at the time, if the conditions for phlebotomy are met, as we have previously mentioned.
If the wound is bleeding, then you should hasten to stop it by sprinkling powdered vitriol on it, if you have nothing else available.
Then proceed to set the fracture on that very same day and do not delay it unless a hot swelling occurs.
If a hot swelling occurs, leave the setting of the fracture until the ninth day until the hot swelling subsides, and do not approach it at all on the third and fourth days, for bad symptoms may arise.
If the broken bone is protruding from the skin and exposed, you should attempt to reduce and align it with your hands gently and with a slight extension.
If you are unable to reduce and align it with your hands, then reduce it with this instrument, which is an instrument made of iron, its length being about seven or eight fingers and its width according to the size of the wound. ولذلك ينبغى للطبيب أن يتّخذ منها ثلاثا او أربعا على قدر ما يحتاج اليه من العلاج فى كلّ نوع من الكسر
And let it be rounded with a slight thickness so that it does not bend when pressed upon during the operation, and let it have a sharp end with a hook at its tip, its upper part being thick and from its middle to the bottom very thin.
And this is its image:
And it is called in Greek "peron" meaning a small lever.
It is necessary that its sharp, curved end be placed on the protruding end of the bone, and push it with it at once, so that when the bone returns and is somewhat leveled, then level the ends of the fracture on each other.
If its broken end is thin and the instrument does not grip it well, it is necessary to cut the end of that bone so that the instrument can grip it.
If you are absolutely unable to reduce the bone with what we have described, then cut it with something similar to the cutters that we mentioned, or saw it with one of the saws however you can.
Then scrape off what remains on the bone of roughness and thin scales.
If you reduce the bone and the patient finds, after its reduction, severe and harmful pain, know that the bone has not returned to its natural position.
If you can return it to its natural position, do so, for you will greatly benefit the patient.
When you have completed your setting of the bone, dip a cloth in a black astringent drink, especially if you are in the summer, and do not put on the wound a cerate nor anything containing fat, lest putrefaction and corruption occur in it.
Then use splints when you have finished setting the bone, and leave the wound uncovered by cutting a hole in the bandages with scissors according to the size of the wound, and beware, with all caution, of tightening the wound with the fracture, for ignorant doctors often do that, causing their patients either death or gangrene or inflammation; and let your tightening be gentle and relaxed, unlike the tightening of the rest of the fracture.
If the wound is bad, or it is a large wound and you fear some of the bad symptoms that we have described, and he finds disturbing pain in the place, it is not necessary to put splints on it; make for it bandages of hard cloths in the place of the splints and tighten it with them.
If it is after a day or two and you see that pus has begun to generate in the wound, remove the cloth that you put on it with the drink, then use the threads and ointments that we are accustomed to treat wounds with, such as the quadruple ointment and the like.
It is necessary for you to loosen the bandage and inspect the wound every day, evening and morning, until it heals and recovers.
It is necessary to position the limb in a way that the pus flows down from it easily.
If many days pass for the wound and it does not heal and the pus does not stop from it, know that there are small bone fragments there, so it is necessary to search the wound with a probe, and whatever of those fragments are loose, extract and remove them, and whatever of them are not loose and are pricking the limb and causing pain, then cut and extract them in every way you can.
If inflammation or gangrene or another type of corruption and putrefaction occurs to the wound, it is necessary to address each symptom of it with something similar to the treatment that was previously described in its chapter.
And among what you should pay attention to my words and keep in mind is if a large bone breaks and protrudes from the limb, such as the femur bone, the humerus bone, and the like of the large limbs, do not attempt to pull it or remove it, for death often results from that, rather leave it until it putrefies, for it may fall off by itself after twenty or thirty days, then at that time treat the wound if you see a place for treatment in it, otherwise leave it.
Chapter Twenty on the treatment of the complication that occurs after some fractures.
This complication often occurs after the healing of a fracture, especially near the joints, which deforms the shape of the limb and may prevent the limb from its natural function.
Look, if the complication is soft, then use astringent medicines in it, such as aloe vera, frankincense, myrrh, spikenard, acacia, and the like, by taking some or all of these and kneading them with an astringent syrup or with egg white or with vinegar, and apply it to the complication in a poultice and tie it tightly and leave the bandage without loosening it for many days, then loosen it and repeat it until the complication is gone, God willing.
Or tighten a plate of sealed lead on it, because lead has a property that removes everything that protrudes in the limbs.
If the complication has hardened and intensified, and necessity urges its removal, then incise it from above and cut off the protruding excess or scrape it with some scrapers until it is gone, and treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter twenty-one on the treatment of a fracture if it has healed and the limb remains.
After that, it becomes thin, unlike its original nature, if the bone fracture heals, and the limb remains thin and weak, then this is due to many reasons, one of which is either due to the frequent loosening of the ligaments and tying them in a way that is not appropriate. وإمّا لإفراط شدّ الرباطات حتّى امتنع الغذاء أن يسرى الى العضو
And the treatment for this is to nourish the patient and enrich his body until the blood increases in it, and to use the bath, and to bring him joy and happiness, and so on.
Then apply tar to the limb so that the tar attracts a lot of nourishment to it, or continue suspending/dangling it with lukewarm water until the nourishment flows into it and it returns to its natural shape.
Chapter Twenty-Two on the Treatment of Broken Bones if They Are Set Crooked ومنعت فعلها على ما ينبغى
So when a limb that has been set after its healing exhibits a curvature or a protrusion of the broken bone, or a knotting, and the appearance of the limb is thus disfigured, but the limb is not prevented from its natural function. فليس ينبغى أن تقبل قول من يزعم أن يكسر العضو من رأس وقد كان كثير من جهّال الأطبّاء والمجبّرين يفعلون ذلك فى بلدنا وهذا الفعل مذموم جدّا يؤدّى الى غرر عظيم أيسره العطب
But if the curvature and knotting are soft, then it should be fomented with water in which softening herbs have been cooked, such as marshmallow leaves and its root, and melilot, and so on, and it should be dressed with softening dressings such as well-made diachylon.
Or marshmallow root mucilage should be taken and mixed with chicken fat and sesame oil, and it should be dressed with it.
Or fatty figs should be taken and pounded with pigeon dung, and similar medications that are called dissolvers of healing.
And the knotting may be dissolved by constant gentle massage done with the hands, and the limb should be moved in all directions at all times.
But if the curvature is old and severe and hardened, and necessity calls for its treatment with iron, then it should be incised at its top and the connection of the bone should be released, and the excess of knotting or bone should be cut with gentle cuts, and gentleness should be employed in this with effort and care.
Then the wound should be treated with what has been mentioned previously until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-Three on the Discussion of the Jaw
The jaw is a joint's dislocation from its place, thus hindering movement, disfiguring the limb, and causing severe aches and pains to the patient.
So when a jaw dislocation occurs to someone, it is necessary to immediately reduce it without any delay, because if it is delayed, the place swells, making it difficult to reduce the jaw.
Therefore, it shouldn't be delayed, moved, or extended while it is swollen because it often causes convulsions and harmful pains to the patient.
But if this happens, it is necessary to immediately phlebotomize the patient, then leave it until the swelling subsides a little, then wash the limb with hot water and oil, then reduce it gently and treat each limb with what will be mentioned in its place.
I have also arranged the chapters on the jaw according to what was previously mentioned regarding fractures, from the top of the body to the bottom.
Chapter Twenty-Four on the Treatment of Dislocation of the Lower Jaw
Rarely do the jaws dislocate except in rare cases.
And their dislocation occurs in one of two ways: إمّا أن يزولا عن مواضعهما زوالا يسيرا فيسترخيا قليلا
So if the dislocation is slight, it may return to its place on its own in most cases with minimal effort.
But if the dislocation is complete, it is necessary to hasten its reduction quickly and not delay it at all.
This is done by having an assistant hold the patient's head, and the physician inserts the thumb of one hand into the base of the jaw inside his mouth if the jaw is dislocated on one side, or inserts both thumbs if the jaw is dislocated on both sides, and with the rest of his fingers on the outside, he adjusts it and orders the patient to relax his jaw and let it go in every direction, and the physician adjusts and pushes the jaw until it returns to its place.
If its reduction is difficult, especially if both jaws are dislocated, use a compress with hot water and oil until their reduction is easy, and do not delay their reduction at all, as we said.
So when they have returned and straightened and the patient's mouth has closed and they do not relax, then place on them pads of cloth with cerate made from wax and rose oil, then tie them gently with a loose bandage.
And the patient should sleep on his back with his head supported between two pillows so that he does not move it right or left and does not strain to chew anything, but makes his food a soft soup. حتّى اذا ذهب الألم وانعقد الفكّ فليأكل ما بدا له
And let him do that gently and not strain to open his mouth when eating, drinking, and yawning until the jaw is firm and healed.
If the reduction of the jaws is difficult when they dislocate at some point and do not return to their places, fevers and persistent headaches often occur from that, and perhaps the patient's bowels loosen, and perhaps he vomits pure bile.
So if you see that, know that he is damaged, and often one who experiences that dies within ten days.
Chapter Twenty-Five on the Reduction of the Dislocation of the Clavicle and the Tip of the Shoulder
As for the clavicle, it does not dislocate from the inner side due to its connection to the chest. وقد تنفكّ الى خارج ويتبيّن ذلك للحسّ
Its treatment is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms, then you press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return.
Then you put on it the bandage and the supports and tighten them.
As for its end, which is next to the shoulder and connected to it, it does not dislocate except rarely. فإن انخلع يوما مّا فينبغى أن يردّ ويسوّى على ما ذكرنا وما يتهيّأ لك
Then put on it the bandage, the supports, and the tightening, and instruct the patient to maintain rest and stillness until he recovers.
With this same treatment, you reduce the end of the shoulder if it also moves from its place.
Chapter Twenty-Six on Reducing a Dislocated Shoulder
Know that the shoulder dislocates in three ways, one of which is that it dislocates downwards towards the armpit
and the second is that it dislocates towards the chest وربّما انفكّ الى فوق المنكب وذلك يكون فى الندرة
and it does not dislocate backwards because of the scapula ولا ينفكّ الى قدّام لمكان العصب
And it mostly dislocates and comes out downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, because it comes out quickly and goes in quickly in them
But as for those who have much flesh, it is the opposite of that, I mean that it comes out with difficulty and goes in with difficulty
And sometimes a person experiences a blow or a fall, and the shoulder swells with a hot swelling, so it is thought that it has dislocated, so it is necessary to examine it until you ascertain its truth, and then proceed with its treatment
The dislocation is recognized, if it is downwards towards the armpit, if you compare the dislocated shoulder with the healthy shoulder, for you will find a clear difference between them, and you will find the head of the shoulder with a curvature, and under the armpit, upon touching, the head of the shoulder is like an egg, and the patient is unable to raise his hand to his ear, nor to move it in all movements
Likewise, if it dislocates towards the chest or upwards, you will find that obvious to the touch, not hidden
This dislocation may be easy to reduce if it is fresh or if the patient is a child
Its reduction is that an assistant raises his hand upwards, then you place your two thumbs under his armpit, and lift the joint forcefully upwards to its place, and the assistant raises his hand and extends it upwards, then lowers it downwards, and it will return quickly
If it does not return by what we have mentioned, and the dislocation has been there for many days, then it is necessary for the patient to bathe in hot water and to use the emollient that softens and relaxes, such as cooking marshmallow root, fenugreek, and melilot in water and using it
Then the patient lies on his back, and you place under his armpit a ball of wool that is moderate between soft and firm, then the physician places his heel on the ball, and holds the patient's hand with his hand, and extends it downwards, and pushes the ball with his foot, and it will return to its place
And if you wish, reduce it in this way, which is that you bring a man taller than the patient and have him stand by the side, and he puts his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lifts his armpit upwards until the patient is suspended in the air, and another assistant pulls the patient's hand down to his lower abdomen, and if the patient is light, then it is necessary to hang something else on him to weigh him down, and the dislocation will return immediately
It may also be reduced in another way, which is to fix a long piece of wood in the ground, the top of which is round like the bottom of a mortar, neither thick nor thin, then it is placed under the patient's armpit after you place a soft cloth on the top of the wood, and the patient is standing along the wood, then you extend his hand downwards from the other side, and he also extends his body from the other side with force, and the joint will return to its place quickly
If its reduction is difficult by all that we have mentioned, then use this treatment, which is to take a piece of wood about two cubits long, four fingers wide, and two fingers thick, with a rounded head to facilitate its entry into the depth of the armpit, in this way:
Then soft rags are tied on the rounded head so that the wood does not harm the patient.
Then it is placed under the armpit and the entire hand and arm are extended on the wood downwards, and the wood is tied on the upper arm, forearm, and the edge of the hand.
Then the arm is placed horizontally on the rung of a ladder and the hand is extended downwards, and the rest of the body is left hanging from the other side, for the joint will enter immediately.
Once it has entered, by whatever means possible, a moderately sized ball of wool should be placed under the armpit. ثمّ يحمل الضماد المهيّأ من غبار الرحى مع اللبان وبياض البيض على المنكب كلّه كما يدور من فوق
Then the ball is tightened firmly from under the armpit, and it is rotated with the bandage on the poultice from above, and his hand is hung to his neck, and he is left without moving his hand for seven days.
And it is necessary that the patient's food be made little until the limb strengthens, for it is faster for his recovery.
Then it is loosened after seven or five days, and he is trained in movement, and if it is stable and does not relax, then he has recovered.
If the joint dislocates frequently due to moisture affecting it or another ailment, then it is necessary to use cauterization with the three needles as mentioned previously in the chapter on cauterization.
If you have done all of this, and loosened the bandage after seven days and the joint did not stabilize, and you repeated the poultice and tightening on it several times, and it did not stabilize and fell and relaxed, and you were unable to raise it upwards, then know that its nerve in the head of the shoulder has been severed, or stretched, or relaxed. فاعلم حينئذ أنّ المفصل لا يثبت فى موضعه أبدا،
As for the dislocation that is towards the chest and breast and backwards, its reduction is by pushing and extending with the hands until it returns.
And all the tightening and treatment is used on it until it heals.
If after healing there appears a stiffness in the limb and slowness in movement, then let the patient use the bath frequently until that stiffness softens and it returns to its original state.
Chapter twenty-seven on the treatment of dislocation of the elbow.
The elbow joint dislocates with difficulty and also returns with difficulty, and it dislocates in all directions, especially forward or backward, and its dislocation is not hidden from you because it is located under the sight and under the touch, in whatever form it is dislocated.
And if you compare the dislocated elbow with the healthy one, this will be clear to you with a clear explanation by the concavity of the joint, and he cannot bend his arm nor touch his shoulder with it.
And it is necessary to hasten and reduce the dislocation immediately before a hot swelling occurs to it, because if a hot swelling occurs to it, it will be difficult to reduce it, and perhaps it will not heal at all, especially if the dislocation is backward, because it is the worst of all types of dislocation and the most severe in pain, and death often occurs with it.
And its treatment, if it is possible to return it, is that an assistant extends his hand with both his hands and his arm outstretched, and the physician's hands are from above the elbow and from below it, and he pushes the joint with both his thumbs or with the base of his palm until it returns to its place.
But if the dislocation is forward, it may be returned by bending the hand suddenly until it strikes with the base of its palm the shoulder that it faces.
If the dislocation does not respond to returning, then use very strong and powerful extension, which is that two assistants extend the arm and two assistants hold the patient so that he does not move during the extension, then the arm is rotated in every direction after wrapping a folded cloth or a wide bandage on his hand.
And when the physician handles the joint with his hands, he wipes it with oil so that it helps in sliding the joint easily, then he pushes the joint strongly until it returns.
And after its return, it is necessary to apply a bandage on it that contains astringent and drying properties with egg white, and tighten it firmly, and suspend the arm from the patient's neck, and leave it for days, then loosen it. If the joint is stable in its place, then loosen the bandage from it and leave it.
And if you see that the joint has not become firm yet, then repeat the bandage and the binding and leave it also for days until it becomes firm, then loosen it.
If stiffness occurs to it after the return of the joint and its loosening and difficulty in movement, then let him use moisturizing in the bath and gentle massage and rubbing until it softens, or place the tail of a fat ram on the joint, then tie it and leave it on him for a day and a night, then remove it and let him enter the bath. فإذا عرق فاعرك المفصل عركا معتدلا ثمّ أعد عليه الألية مرّة وثانية وثالثة مع دخول الحمّام حتّى يلين،
And if you want to put on it fresh, soft cow dung with ghee and tighten it on him, do that several times, because it will soften and return to its original state.
Chapter twenty-eight on the treatment of dislocation of the wrist.
The wrist joint frequently dislocates.
And the reduction of its dislocation is easy, unlike other joints. إلّا أنّه ينبغى أن يسرع بردّ فكّه الساعة التى ينفكّ فيها قبل أن يرم الموضع او يعرض فيه ورم حارّ.
And the reduction of its dislocation is that you place the wrist of the ill person on a board and an assistant extends his hand and the physician places his palm on the prominence of the joint and pushes it until it returns.
Except that it is necessary to look, if the dislocation has shifted towards the inside of the hand, then let the ill person place the back of his hand on the board during the extension and reduction. وإن كان الفكّ بارزا الى ظاهر اليد فليكن وضع يده الباطنة على اللوح لتقع يد الطبيب على نفس نتو المفصل.
And if it returns immediately (well and good), otherwise tighten it with a bandage that soothes the swelling and leave it, do not return to it, because it does not bear it, and you will not be able to reduce it after days have passed for it.
Except that the joint remains in its crookedness and does not harm the ill person at all, except if the hand becomes loose and is unable to grasp anything. فحينئذ تعلم أنّ العصب انقطع او ترضّض فلا حيلة فيه إلّا أن يشدّ بالكىّ فربّما نفع وربّما لم ينفع ذلك شيئا.
So if the reduction of the wrist is completed, then apply to it the bandage that we described, then it is tightened and left for five days, then it is loosened, and the hand is exercised.
And if its movement is difficult and some stiffness occurs in it, then soften it with heated water and rubbing repeatedly until it softens.
Chapter twenty-nine on the treatment of dislocated fingers.
Fingers may dislocate in any direction.
So when a finger dislocates to the back or palm of the hand, extend the finger and push the dislocation with your thumb until it returns (to its place).
Then, bind the tip of the finger and suspend it towards the direction to which it was dislocated and leave it for two days, then release it and extend it until it straightens itself on that day.
If you tied it at night in the same manner, continue to untie it during the day and exercise it with movement and tie it at night, doing that for several days until it strengthens.
And do the same with it if it dislocates towards the palm of the hand, tie it towards the same direction and do with it what you did before until it heals.
And do the same with it whenever it dislocates in any other direction.
Chapter Thirty on the Treatment of Dislocation of the Vertebrae of the Back
When a vertebra of the back or neck is completely dislocated, or many vertebrae are displaced from their positions, there is no treatment for it because death comes quickly to the patient,
And a sign of this is that the patient's stool comes out involuntarily, he cannot hold it, and often some of his limbs become relaxed, either his legs or his arms, or one of them.
But if one vertebra is displaced from its position, it often shifts, and its shifting can be in four directions, and the one that shifts backward is called a hump.
And as for its treatment, you should observe: if the hump occurred from childhood, there is no treatment for it, nor any cure at all.
But as for the one that occurred from a fall or a blow and the like, the ancients mentioned it with various kinds of treatment in lengthy discourse, most of which is not beneficial, and I have summarized from that what little suffices for much of what they brought, from my approaching the meaning and my explanation of it, and I have depicted the instrument differently from what they explained and illustrated.
So I say that the hump that occurs from the front in the chest, there is no remedy for it, nor any cure from it, and likewise the one that is to the two sides also, but only the one that occurs in the back is treated, especially with what I am describing.
It is that you lay the patient on his face on a level bench near a wall and spread a soft padding under him so that his chest is not harmed, then you place a standing plank planted in a hole in the ground at the end of the bench towards his head, and another plank towards his feet at the other end of the bench, and an assistant holds the plank, and let it not be fixed in the hole, and another assistant holds the other in that manner, then you wrap around the patient's chest and under his armpits with a soft, tight bandage and extend the end of the bandage to the plank that is at his head and tie it there, then you tighten with another bandage over his hips and over his knees and at his ankles, then you gather all the bandages and tie them to the other plank that is at his feet, then each assistant pulls the plank towards his side with the bandage, and the two planks do not move from their planted positions except that they are not fixed as we said, and the physician places his palms on the vertebra with force until it returns, or he places a board on it, then he leans on the board with his feet until it returns.
If it does not return with this treatment, then you take a board whose length is about three cubits and dig in the wall that we said should be near the patient a place into which the end of the board is inserted, then you place the middle of the board on the hump, and the physician places his feet on the other end and pulls well until he presses the vertebra and it returns to its place.
And if you wish to do it with the screw that is turned by hand, it is that you plant in the ground at the patient's head at the end of the bench two planks whose length is a cubit, and at his feet at the end of the bench also two planks, and let the distance between each plank be a span, and a hole has been made in each plank in which the screw runs, and all the planks are well fixed in the ground so that they do not move at all, and you insert a rounded stick, which is the screw in which the bandage is twisted, into the holes of the two planks, and at its end is a hole in which a stick a span long has been fixed with what it twists, and in the other two planks the same.
Then you tighten the bandage that you tightened on the patient's chest in the screw that is at his head, and the bandages that you tightened on his legs in the screw that is at his feet.
Then an assistant stands at each screw, turning his hand with the turner with which the screw is twisted, and the physician straightens the hump as we have described.
And this is a picture of the screw, the bench, and the patient:
Then, after the vertebra returns and the place becomes level, it is necessary to apply the dried dressing with egg white. ثمّ المشاقة
Then it is tied with the appropriate bandage, and the patient uses light food until he recovers.
If some protrusion remains in the place at the end of the healing, it is necessary to use the medicines that relax and soften, along with the use of the board that we described for a long time. وقد تستعمل فى ذلك صفيحة رصاص
And a protrusion may appear at the end of the vertebrae of the back, and it is thought to be a dislocation, and it is an extra bone that has protruded, so do not treat it with this treatment, for death may occur.
Chapter thirty-one on the treatment of dislocated hip.
Know that the hip joint and the shoulder joint are only subject to dislocation, and they are not subject to what happens to other joints of slight displacement and concavity.
And the hip joint dislocates in four ways, that is, it dislocates inward, outward, forward, and backward, and it most often dislocates inward, and rarely dislocates forward or backward.
And the sign of its dislocation inward is that if you compare the healthy leg of the patient with the diseased one, it will be longer, and the knee will be more prominent than the healthy one, and the patient will not be able to bend his leg at the groin, and the area next to the groin will be swollen, a clear swelling, because the head of the femur has gone there.
And the sign of that which is subject to dislocation outward is that its symptoms are the opposite of these symptoms.
And the sign of that which is subject to dislocation forward is that he extends his leg completely, except that he cannot bend it without pain being in the knee, and if he intends to walk, he cannot do so forward, and he retains his urine, and his groin swells, and when walking, his weight is on his heel.
And the sign of that which is subject to dislocation backward is that he does not extend the knee, and he cannot bend it before he bends the groin, and his leg is also shorter than the other, and the groin is relaxed, and the head of the femur is clearly at the position of the loin.
As for the reduction of the types of this dislocation, it is that you look; if the dislocation is old, it has become chronic with its owner, and he has not tried to reduce it, and it has remained in its state, then there is no treatment at all, so you should not deal with it.
As for he whose dislocation is recent, and whatever type it may be of the four ways of dislocation, hasten to twist the joint and extend it inward and outward and move it right and left, perhaps it will return and will not need any other treatment.
If it does not return like this, then you should prepare a strong servant who will extend his leg from below, either with his hands or with a bandage tied around his leg above the knee, and another servant will extend him from above by putting his hands under his armpits, then he will tighten a soft bandage on the origin of the thigh, and a third servant will hold the end of the bandage, and his extension will be either from the front from the groin to the collarbone or from the back to the back.
And their extension will all be at once until the patient is raised from the ground with his body and remains suspended.
For this type of extension is a common type for the four types.
If the dislocation returns as we said, otherwise, each type must have the special treatment that I mention.
As for its special reduction if the dislocation is inward, the patient should lie on his healthy side, then you place a bandage on the origin of the thigh between the head of the femur and the area under the groin, then you extend the bandage upward from the groin to the upper body to the collarbone, then another strong servant takes with his arms and embraces the thick area of the diseased thigh and extends it outward with a strong pull, then it returns to its place.
And this type is easier than the other types of treatment by which this limb is reduced.
If it is difficult for you and it does not respond to entering with this type of treatment at all, then you should tie the patient's legs together with a strong, soft bandage on the heels and on the knees, and the distance between each one of them should be the length of four fingers, and the diseased leg should be extended more than the other by the length of two fingers.
Then the patient is suspended from the head by a wooden beam that is in the house, and its distance from the ground is the length of two arms, then you order a strong boy to embrace the head of the femur, and another boy will hold onto the patient, and the other boy who is embracing the femur will push strongly, then the joint returns to its place quickly.
As for its special reduction if the dislocation is outward, the patient should lie on the bench according to what we described for the hunchback, and tighten the bandage on his diseased leg especially and on his chest, then two wooden beams are placed, one at his feet and the other at his head, then an additional wooden beam is placed in the middle of the bench, very securely fastened, with a wet cloth wrapped around it so as not to hurt the patient, so that the beam is between his thighs so that he does not be pulled downward during the extension.
Then each servant extends to his side and the physician straightens the hip with his hands.
If it responds to the return, otherwise, place the board on him and compress it as we mentioned in the hunchback, except that the patient should lie on his healthy side.
And if the dislocation is forward, then you should extend the patient's leg at once, while he is in this very description on the bench, and the physician places the palm of his right hand on the diseased groin, then he presses it with the other hand, and with that, the pressure is extended downward to the knee.
And if the dislocation is backward, it should not be extended downward while it is raised from the ground, but it should be placed on something solid, as it should also be if his hip is dislocated outward, according to what we mentioned of his lying on the bench, and he is on his face, and the bandages are tightened as we said before, and the compression with the board should also be used on the place where the joint came out.
When the hip joint returns completely as it should, and the sign of its return will not be hidden from you, which is that you extend the patient's legs; if you see them level and the patient grasps and extends the leg without difficulty, then know that the limb has returned as it should. Then, bring the thighs together, apply the bandage, and tighten it with a turban so tightly that the hip does not move to any side, and the patient must remain still for three or four days, then untie the bandage, and compare the leg with the other.
If you see them equal in size, then know that the dislocation has healed, so allow the patient to walk.
And if you see some relaxation in it, then return and bandage it and tighten it according to your first tightening and leave it for three days as well, then untie it and let him walk slowly on it for days until it strengthens well, God willing.
Chapter thirty-two on the treatment of knee dislocation.
The knee dislocates in three directions: it dislocates inwards, outwards, and downwards, I mean backwards, and it does not dislocate forwards at all.
And the sign of its dislocation is that you order the patient to bring his leg to his thigh, and if it does not stick to the thigh, then know that the knee is dislocated.
And the treatment of all its dislocations is that you sit the patient down, having extended his legs, if he is able to do that, and you sit a servant behind him to hold his waist and twist it backwards a little, then you sit on his thighs, putting your back to his face, and you put his leg between your legs, then you grasp his knee with your palms, interlocking them between your fingers on his knee, then you squeeze both sides of his knee with your palms strongly, and another servant extends his leg until the knee returns to its place.
And the sign of its return is that the leg sticks to the thigh softly, without force.
Then bandage it, and stick the leg to the thigh, then bind them both with a bandage for three or four days, then release them.
And he should not engage in anything except a little walking for some days, until it strengthens.
If its return is difficult for you with what we described, otherwise, use strong extension with the bandages that I previously described for the treatment of the hip, until it returns.
Chapter thirty-three on the treatment of dislocated heel.
The heel bone may be slightly displaced. وقد ينفكّ على الكمال
The sign of its dislocation is that you see the heel bone swollen, protruding towards the side to which it has been dislocated.
As for the treatment of its slight displacement, it is easy to reduce. وهو أن يمدّ برفق بالأيدى ويسوّى حتّى يرجع
As for its treatment if it is completely dislocated فينبغى أن تجلس العليل قاعدا
Then you take hold of his foot with your right hand from above and with your left hand from below his foot at the ankle.
Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand then with your left hand twice.
Then extend it with the left hand and push the dorsum of the foot with the right hand towards the leg without force, you do this twice as we have described.
Then push the dorsum of the foot to the leg on the third time while you pull at the ankle.
If it returns (to its place) in one or two times in this manner and you see the foot leveled
otherwise repeat the procedure, it will return.
If its return is prevented using what we have described وإلّا فأضجع العليل على ظهره على الأرض وأغرز وتدا فى الأرض موثّقا جدّا ليقع بين فخذيه وقد لففت عليه خرقا لئلّا يؤذى العليل
Then an assistant secures his thigh. ثمّ يمدّ خادم آخر الرجل إمّا بيديه وإمّا برباط يربطه على عنق الرجل
Then the physician sets the dislocation with his hands and another assistant holds the healthy leg down. فإنّ الفكّ يرجع بسرعة
So when the dislocation returns and you are certain of its return, apply the bandage and the splint and tighten it with firm bandages and tie the foot with the bandage downwards.
It is necessary to avoid the tendon that is above the heel from behind so that the bandage is not tight on it and harms it.
Then leave it for two or three days. If the bandage loosens, tighten it.
Then release it on the third or fourth day. ويمتنع العليل من المشى أربعين يوما
If he experiences a hot swelling, it is necessary to use in its soothing what we have previously described in another place of treatment and softening until it disappears.
Chapter thirty-four on the treatment of dislocation of the toes.
It is appropriate that you straighten what has become dislocated from it with a gentle extension, without violence, and this is not difficult, but easy.
If the dislocation is in some of the joints of the back of the foot, then it is appropriate that the patient place his foot on a level place on the ground or on a board while he is standing like someone walking.
Then stand yourself and place your foot on what protrudes from those joints, then tread on it with your foot with force until it returns and you see that it has straightened, and no protrusion appears in the place.
Then place under the sole of his foot a board that takes the whole foot, which has two ends, then tighten it with a tight and firm binding for three days, then loosen it and protect him from walking for many days until it strengthens and you are assured of no recurrence, God willing.
Chapter Thirty-Five: On the types of jaw dislocation that occurs with a wound or with a fracture or with both of them.
Whenever something like this happens, and you intend to treat it and fix it, it often results in death.
Therefore, no one should attempt to treat such a thing except someone who is skilled in the craft, long-experienced, gentle, compassionate, deliberate, neither reckless nor daring.
And he should use, in the beginning, only the medicines that soothe hot swellings and entrust the sick person to fate - God willing - except for what you hope for his safety from damage, along with the mildness of the illness and you see in it some hope.
So send him away immediately at the beginning of the matter before the hot swelling occurs, and if the limb returns to what you wanted, then use the regimen that soothes hot swellings and treat the wound with appropriate drying ointments.
If the jaw is fractured and bone fragments that are loose occur, then extract them and follow in that what we mentioned in simple diseases from what preceded in their places.
And strive your utmost and keep yourself from entering the path of risks, as I have previously advised you, for that is more preserving of your prestige and safer for your honor, God willing.
